The blame subprocess runs **once per file** (off-thread, re-run only on the coarse `applyGitState` events ‚Äî tab switch / focus / save / mutation) and only the active buffer is annotated; there is no per-keystroke/per-caret work (the old per-caret `BlameOverlay` canvas was removed). **The whole inline-blame feature lives in `GitCoordinator`** ‚Äî the engine (`applyBlame`/`refreshBlame`/`toBlameInfos`) *and* the UI (`toggleBlame`/`blameShowCommit`/`onGutterBlameClick`); `MainController` just registers the commands (delegating to `git::toggleBlame`/`git::blameShowCommit`) and wires the gutter click (`buffer.setGutterBlameClick(git::onGutterBlameClick)`). The two surfaces the UI touches outside the coordinator route through `WindowOps`: `syncBlameCheck()` (the Settings checkbox) and `openCommitFileDiff(hash, repoRel)` (the line's commit diff ‚Äî through the window to reach `DiffCoordinator` without a circular dependency). Gated by `Settings.gitBlameInline` (default off; schema 20‚Üí21 additive-identity; `git.toggleBlame`/`M-g a`; Settings ‚Üí Git checkbox + `SettingsWindow.syncGitBlameCheck`). `git.blameShowCommit` opens the caret line's commit diff; clicking any line's annotation opens that line's. CSS `.blame-slot`/`.blame-author`/`.blame-date`/`.blame-tooltip` in `app.css` (semantic colors, theme-tracking). **Stash** commands (`git.stash` with an optional message prompt, `git.stashPop`, `git.unstash`/`git.stashDrop` over a `QuickOpen<StashEntry>` picker) plus **Stash/Unstash** rows in the `BranchPopup` actions list. All gated by `gitEnabled()` (so disabled in Simple UI mode); `git.*`/`tool.gitLog` are palette-filtered when Git is off. *Deferred (later phase): a richer log graph/filtering, live-as-you-type gutter diff vs the HEAD blob, interactive rebase/merge/tag UIs.*
- `diff/` ‚Äî **Diff viewer + merge-conflict resolution** (SDD-driven). Pure, unit-tested core on **java-diff-utils** (`io.github.javadiffutils`, an automatic module ‚Äî moditect injects a descriptor for the jlink dist, like pdfbox; deps only `java.base`, not signed so no strip). No diff-match-patch: its Maven artifact isn't a reliable JPMS module, so intra-line word highlighting is done in-house. **`DiffEngine.compute(left, right)` ‚Üí `DiffModels.DiffModel`** walks the java-diff-utils `Patch` deltas into aligned **side-by-side rows** (`Row{type EQUAL/ADDED/REMOVED/MODIFIED, left, leftLine, right, rightLine, leftWordRanges, rightWordRanges}` ‚Äî a CHANGE delta is paired line-by-line into MODIFIED rows + filler for the longer side) plus derived **unified rows** and `changeBlockStarts` (prev/next nav); `lines(text)` normalizes CRLF + drops one trailing newline. **`compute(left, right, DiffOptions{ignoreWhitespace, wordLevel})`** is the options overload (drives the File History tool window's inline-diff toggles): `ignoreWhitespace` runs the Myers diff over whitespace-normalized lines but ‚Äî since normalization is strictly 1:1 per line ‚Äî the delta positions still index the originals, so every `Row` renders the **original** text (only equality changes); `wordLevel=false` skips the per-line `InlineDiff` (whole-line highlight). `DiffService` gained a matching options overload. **`InlineDiff`** tokenizes a changed line into word/non-word runs, diffs the token lists, and maps changed tokens back to `[start,end)` char ranges (word-level emphasis, no second lib). **`ConflictParser`** parses Git markers (`<<<<<<<`/`|||||||`/`=======`/`>>>>>>>`) ‚Üí ours/**base**/theirs segments (the 3-way `|||||||` common-ancestor region is **captured** when present ‚Äî i.e. `diff3`/`zdiff3` `merge.conflictStyle`; empty under Git's default `merge` style, gated via `Conflict.hasBase()`/`ConflictFile.hasBase()`) + `resolve(file, choices)` (OURS/THEIRS/**BASE**/BOTH/UNRESOLVED-keeps-markers, where UNRESOLVED round-trips the captured base region verbatim). **`PatchWriter.unifiedDiff`** ‚Üí a `.patch` via `UnifiedDiffUtils`; the reverse direction, **`PatchParser.parse(text)`**, is a pure/unit-tested parser that reconstructs each file section's old/new line sequences from a unified diff (tolerant of a bare `diff -u` file, a git `diff --git`/`index`/rename preamble, several files back to back, `/dev/null` add/delete sides, and a `\ No newline at end of file` marker; a hunk's declared `@@ -a,b +c,d @@` line counts gate exactly how many lines are consumed as content, so a removed/added line that happens to start with `---`/`+++` is never mistaken for the next file's header). The reconstructed lines feed straight back into `DiffEngine.compute` ‚Äî no new row type needed. **`DiffCoordinator.openPatchFile(buffer)`** opens the active `.patch`/`.diff` buffer's first file-section as a read-only structured diff tab this way (via the tab-menu **"Open in Diff Viewer"** item ‚Äî shown only for a `.patch`/`.diff` file ‚Äî or the palette-only `diff.openPatchFile`); it parses the buffer's own live text (not a re-read from disk), so unsaved edits to the patch are reflected, and reports a status note when the patch has more than one file (v1 shows just the first). **`DiffService`** runs `DiffEngine` off the FX thread (the `GitService` idiom; posts `null` past a 60k-line guard). **UI** (`ui/`): **`DiffViewerPane implements TabContent`** ‚Äî side-by-side (default) is two read-only `editor-area` `CodeArea`s with synced vertical scroll (guarded `estimatedScrollYProperty` listeners; aligned row counts mean equal line heights), per-side original-line-number gutters (`setParagraphGraphicFactory`), TextMate syntax (`TextMateHighlighter.compute`) **overlaid** with intra-line `.diff-word` spans (`StyleSpans.overlay`), and per-line diff backgrounds via `setParagraphStyle` (`.diff-added/-removed/-modified/-filler`); a toolbar toggles **unified** (one CodeArea, `+/‚àí` gutter), navigates prev/next change, and exports the patch. The toolbar's view-toggle / apply-all / prev / next actions are also **palette commands** `diff.toggleView`/`diff.applyAll`/`diff.nextChange`/`diff.previousChange` (via `DiffCoordinator.withActiveDiff` over the active tab's `DiffViewerPane`; `applyAllChanges()` no-ops on a read-only diff). **`MergeViewerPane implements TabContent`** lists each conflict (ours/theirs `TextArea`s ‚Äî plus a middle **base** column with an **Accept Base** button when the conflict `hasBase()`, styled `.merge-base`) with Accept Ours/Theirs/Both + a resolved-count toolbar; Save routes the resolved lines back (replaces the active buffer text, undoable). **`Icons.diff()`/`merge()`** + `.diff-*`/`.merge-*` CSS in `app.css`. **The whole diff/merge feature lives in `ui/DiffCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern ‚Äî owns the `DiffService`, `openDiff`/`refreshOpenDiffs`/`withActiveDiff`, the `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` "apply change" flow, `worktreeText`, `exportPatch`, the compare entry points, and `resolveConflicts`; git-backed diffs reach the repo via the shared `GitCoordinator` passed in; reaches the window via an `Ops` extension for add-diff-tab / open-buffer-for-path / open-background-buffer / save-buffer / the open-&-active diff-pane lookups / finder-start-dir). `computeDiff` + `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` are **package-visible** so the Local File History tool window (`FileHistoryPanel`, via `HistoryCoordinator`) reuses them for its inline revision diff + per-hunk chevrons, and `applyToLocal` also lets History's `restoreHistory` write a restored revision through the same undoable-buffer path. **The Local File History feature itself lives in `ui/HistoryCoordinator`** (the same `CoordinatorHost` pattern) ‚Äî it owns the `HistoryService` (off-thread snapshot/blob engine) + the `FileHistoryPanel`, the record hooks (save/autosave/external/pre-delete), the per-file + folder-history views, the label / recent-changes pickers, and the revision diff/restore (via the shared `DiffCoordinator`), reaching the window via an `Ops` extension (the `history/index.json` bucket maps + save / blobs dir / the File History tool-window availability+open / open-path / tree-refresh / current-text). **The revision diff lives inline in the tool window** (there is no separate history window ‚Äî the old `ui/LocalHistoryWindow` was folded in): `FileHistoryPanel` is a horizontal `SplitPane` ‚Äî the revision `ListView` (+ label/reason/time filter) on the left, and on the right a **live** side-by-side diff of the *selected* revision (before) vs the current file (after), rebuilt on selection by re-diffing off-thread via the injected `FileHistoryPanel.DiffSupport` (‚Üí `DiffCoordinator.computeDiff`) into a reused `DiffViewerPane` (its own toolbar keeps side-by-side/unified + prev/next). A right-pane toolbar shows the revision-timestamp header, an **N-differences** count (`model.changeBlockStarts().size()`), **Ignore whitespace** / **Highlight words** `ToggleButton`s (both `recompute()` via `DiffEngine.DiffOptions`), and a **Revert** button (‚Üí `restoreHistory`, undoable). The diff's current-file (RIGHT) side is **editable**, so the IntelliJ-style **per-hunk apply chevrons** do selective restore (a fragment from the snapshot into the file through the undoable buffer, via `DiffSupport.applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal`); after an apply/undo the panel re-baselines (`currentText`) and re-diffs so the remaining chevrons update (`reDiffAfterEdit`). No diff runs until a revision is selected (nothing when the window is closed / no selection), and the right pane resets to a "select a revision" prompt on tab switch / new file. `DiffSupport` is injected once by `HistoryCoordinator.setDiffSupport` (delegating to `historyService.content` / `diff.*` / `ops.currentTextOf` / `host.settings` / `restoreHistory`); folder-history mode keeps the tree on the left with the right pane disabled (its revisions belong to different files). `MainController` keeps the File History `ToolWindow` (built with `historyCoordinator.panel()`) + the `history.*`/`tool.fileHistory` command registrations + the project-tree "Show Local History" item (delegating to the coordinator). `MainController` keeps the `diff.*`/`merge.resolve` command registrations + the tab-menu / Git-panel / project-tree / Git-log entry points (delegating to the coordinator), and calls `diffCoordinator.refreshOpenDiffs()` on window focus-regain + in `afterGitMutation`. Entry points: `diff.vsHead` (`C-x v =`; tab menu "Compare with HEAD"; Git-panel "Show Diff" ‚Üí `diffGitPanelFile(rel, staged)` = staged: index‚ÜîHEAD, unstaged: working‚Üîindex), `diff.compareWith` (FileFinder picks the second file ‚Äî **ungated**), `diff.vsCommit` (`QuickOpen` over `GitService.log`), `merge.resolve` (opens the merge view when `ConflictParser.hasConflictMarkers`). Git-backed diffs are `ifGit`-gated; the working side uses the open buffer's live text when the file is open (canonical-path match), else disk (`worktreeText`, which decodes a closed file's bytes with the same charset rules as the blob side, not force-UTF-8). **Both a blob and a closed working file decode with the file's real charset** (`EditorConfigCharset.resolveName(bytes, ops.editorConfigCharset(file))` ‚Üí `decode`: a BOM wins, else the file's `.editorconfig` `charset`, else UTF-8 ‚Äî mirroring how the editor reads the file), so a Latin-1/UTF-16 tracked file shows real text and only genuine edits differ instead of UTF-8 mojibake + a spurious whole-file change (#435). **Live refresh**: each side is a re-fetchable `DiffSide` (a `Consumer<Consumer<String>>` ‚Äî a `git show` blob via the `blobSide(root, spec, file)` helper, or `worktreeText`), and `openDiff` installs a `DiffViewerPane.refresher` that re-fetches both + `pane.updateContent(...)` **only when the content changed** (`pane.matches(l,r)` guard, so an unchanged refresh keeps the view + scroll); `refreshOpenDiffs()` (iterates tabs whose `userData instanceof DiffViewerPane`) runs on **window focus-regain** (a compared file changed on disk) and in **`afterGitMutation`** (a commit/stage/checkout moved HEAD/index/working). **Apply change** (IntelliJ's hunk-accept arrow): `DiffViewerPane.setEditable(EditableSide, onApply)` marks which side is the writable local file (RIGHT for vs-HEAD/vs-commit/unstaged, LEFT for compare-with, NONE for staged index‚ÜîHEAD); that side's gutter then shows apply chevrons (`.diff-apply`): a **single chevron on every changed row** (per-line / sub-hunk ‚Äî `applyRow` ‚Üí `computeApplied(i,i+1)`) and a **double chevron at each change block's first row** (whole hunk ‚Äî `applyBlock(start)` ‚Üí `computeApplied(start, blockEndFrom(start))`), both over the pure aligned rows; an **Apply-all** toolbar button (`Icons.check()`, shown only when a side is editable) replaces the editable file with the other side wholesale. Both hand the new full text to `DiffCoordinator.applyToLocal(target, text)` ‚Äî which routes through an **undoable editor buffer** (`bufferForApply`: the open buffer, else one opened in the **background** via `addBuffer(buffer, false)` so the diff stays focused), `replaceText`s it (marks dirty), then `refreshOpenDiffs()` re-diffs. The toolbar's **Undo** (`undoLocal` ‚Üí the buffer's `undo()`) and **Save** (`saveLocal` ‚Üí `save(buffer)`) act on that buffer, so applies are revertible and persisted explicitly. **Apply-all** confirms first (it replaces the whole file). (`setEditable` rebuilds the view so the arrows + Undo/Save/Apply-all toolbar buttons appear, since it runs after construction.) **One new dependency + its moditect entry; no `module-info` opens / Settings / schema change.** *Deferred: a **computed** 3-way merge ‚Äî fetch base/ours/theirs (the conflicted index stages `:1:`/`:2:`/`:3:` via `GitService.show`, or `git merge-base` + blobs outside a conflict) and run a diff3 engine that auto-resolves non-conflicting hunks and surfaces only true conflicts, independent of the user's `conflictStyle` (the base **column** itself already ships ‚Äî see `MergeViewerPane`/`ConflictParser` ‚Äî but it's only populated for `diff3`/`zdiff3` markers); in-diff editing, gutter-arrow stage/revert hunks, the SDD's standalone Diff Model persistence, multi-file `.patch` tabs (one tab per file section).*
- `process/` + `mermaid/` ‚Äî **Mermaid diagram support** (on by default ‚Äî inert until the `mmdc` CLI is detected ‚Äî gated by `Settings.mermaidSupport`). The generic subprocess runner `ProcessRunner` lives in **`com.editora.process`** (moved out of `git/` so Git and Mermaid share it; `GitService` passes `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` through the new `run(dir,timeout,cmd,extraEnv)` overload, and `LC_ALL=C` is always set). **GUI-launch PATH fix (important):** a Finder-launched `.app` (or a `.desktop`) inherits a stripped `PATH` (`/usr/bin:/bin:‚Ä¶`) without Homebrew/npm/Node dirs, so `mmdc`/`npx`/`maid` (and a Homebrew `git`) wouldn't be found ‚Äî `ProcessRunner` builds an **augmented PATH** = the inherited PATH **+ the user's login-shell PATH + the usual install dirs**, then rewrites a bare command name to its absolute path against it before launching (Java's Unix `ProcessBuilder` resolves the executable against the JVM's own stripped PATH, not the child env, so both steps are needed). The **login-shell PATH** (`ProcessRunner.loginShellPath()`) is the crucial part for version managers: it runs the user's `$SHELL -l -i -c 'printf ‚Ä¶$PATH‚Ä¶'` **once** (stdin `/dev/null`, stderr discarded, 5 s timeout, markers fence the PATH off from any rc banner ‚Äî the pure marker parse `extractMarked` is unit-tested; the VS Code `resolveShellEnv` approach) and folds its entries in. This recovers bin dirs that are **version-specific and so can't be hardcoded** ‚Äî e.g. **nvm**'s `~/.nvm/versions/node/<ver>/bin` (where npm-global servers like `typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`yaml-language-server` live), fnm/asdf/volta, and a profile-set Homebrew. The hardcoded `EXTRA_PATH_DIRS` (`/opt/homebrew/bin`, `/usr/local/bin`, `/opt/local/bin`, `~/.local/bin`, `~/go/bin`, `~/.cargo/bin`, ‚Ä¶) remain as a fallback. `augmentedPath()` is cached after the first call, and `LspManager`'s constructor **warms it off-thread** (the probe spawns a process) so neither detection nor the FX-thread `session.start()` blocks. Windows yields no login-shell PATH (no POSIX convention). A Settings absolute path still overrides. `com.editora.mermaid.Mermaid` is the static CLI facade over **mmdc** (mermaid-cli; renders/exports) and **maid** (`probelabs/maid`; a fast pure-JS linter): `renderPng(mmdc,source,dark)` (writes a temp `.mmd`, runs `mmdc -i -o -t default|dark -b transparent -s 2`, reads the **PNG** ‚Äî *not* SVG, because JavaFX/JSVG can't apply mermaid's embedded `<style>` CSS or render its `<foreignObject>` HTML labels, so SVG comes out all-black/textless; mmdc rasterizes faithfully via headless Chromium), `exportTo(...)` (format by the chosen file extension ‚Äî SVG/PNG/PDF, mmdc writes it directly), `validate(maid,source)` (runs `maid --format json`, parsed by the pure, unit-tested `MaidOutput` ‚Üí `Diagnostic{line,column,severity,code,message}`; JSON with a text fallback). `MermaidService` (UI-owned, mirrors `GitService`: daemon executor + `Platform.runLater` + cached availability probe) backs the export command + the Settings detection status. Because `MarkdownRenderer` is synchronous/pure but mmdc is a multi-second subprocess, the editor-side **`MermaidImages`** static fa√ßade (like `PreviewImageLoader`: daemon pool + cache, configured via `configure(enabled,mmdcExe,maidExe,dark)` injected from `MermaidCoordinator.applySupport`) returns a placeholder `StackPane` immediately and fills it async ‚Äî decoding mmdc's PNG with a JavaFX `Image` (logical width = pixels √∑ `RENDER_SCALE`) into an `ImageView` sized by a caller-supplied `DoubleUnaryOperator` (embedded Markdown blocks clamp to the content column; a standalone `.mmd` multiplies by the preview zoom so zoom actually resizes the image) ‚Äî **cached by `sha-256(source+theme)`** so the debounced whole-document re-render never re-invokes mmdc for unchanged diagrams; on failure it shows `maid`'s precise line/column diagnostics (else mmdc's stderr) in a `.mermaid-error` label. (No JSVG/AWT in the Mermaid path ‚Äî PNG decodes natively.) `MarkdownRenderer` special-cases a fenced block whose info string is `mermaid` (`isMermaidInfo`) ‚Üí `MermaidImages.node(...)`, else the usual `codeBlock`. Standalone **`.mmd` files** (TextMate grammar `grammars/mermaid.tmLanguage.json` ‚Üí `source.mermaid`, `LanguageRegistry` `mmd`‚Üí`mermaid`) get the same 3-mode preview: `EditorBuffer.isDiagram()`/`hasPreview()` generalize the markdown gating, and `scheduleRenderPreview` branches to render the whole buffer as one diagram. **Markwhen timelines** (`.mw`/`.markwhen` ‚Üí language `markwhen`, scope `source.markwhen`, authored `grammars/markwhen.tmLanguage.json`) get the same 3-mode preview via the identical seam: the pure, JavaFX-free **`com.editora.markwhen`** package (`MwDate` ‚Äî ISO + English month-name dates as half-open `[start,endExclusive)` intervals; sealed `MwNode` `Event`/`Group`; `Timeline`; tolerant line-based `MarkwhenParser.parse` ‚Äî frontmatter `title:`/`#Tag: color`, `#`-header sections nested by level like Markdown, single/range events split on a whitespace-surrounded `-`/`/`, `//` comments ‚Äî all unit-tested) parses the buffer **off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`** (a fourth `scheduleRenderPreview` branch beside `isMarkwhen()`, `previewGen` stale-guard) and **`editor/MarkwhenTimeline.build(model, zoomScale, viewportWidth)`** renders it on the FX thread as a **node-based `Pane`** (time axis + tick gridlines, one row per event/group, range‚Üírounded `Region` bar / point‚Üí`Circle`, `#`-section bands, hover tooltips, `#tag` colors from the frontmatter else a fallback palette; capped at 500 events ‚Üí placeholder), themed via `.markwhen-*` AtlantaFX looked-up colors in `app.css` (no per-theme override). Folding reuses the Markdown heading-level algorithm (`FoldRegions.markwhen`, `headingLevel` ignores space-less `#tag:` decls); `Commenter` `//`; `FileIcons` `table` glyph; horizontal zoom scales the axis width (re-render via `applyPreviewScale`). **A second renderer ‚Äî `editor/MarkwhenCalendar` (month-grid: a vertical stack of Sun‚ÄìSat month cards, tag-colored event chips on each covered day, capped at 120 months) ‚Äî is toggled per file** (`EditorBuffer.MarkwhenView` TIMELINE/CALENDAR, `toggleMarkwhenView`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.markwhenViews`; the render branch picks the renderer); both share `editor/MarkwhenPaint` (tag‚Üícolor). The Markwhen preview right-click menu (and palette `markwhen.exportJson`/`markwhen.toggleView`) offers **Export to JSON** (`markwhen/MarkwhenJson.toJson` ‚Äî a clean pretty-printed tree of title/tagColors/nested nodes, not `@markwhen/parser`'s schema) and **Switch to Calendar/Timeline View**, plus **Export to PDF** and **Print** (both a light raster snapshot of the timeline/calendar ‚Äî the shared preview‚ÜíPDF/print snapshot path, see the *snapshot preview export* note in `pdf/` above). Word (docx/odt) stays markwhen-unsupported (`isMarkdown()`-only). Deferred: relative/human-fuzzy dates, recurrence, times/timezones, lane-packing, and a markwhen CLI (none renders to an image like `mmdc`). Command `mermaid.export` (`FileChooser` SVG/PNG/PDF ‚Üí `MermaidService.export`). Each tool is run as a **tokenized command** (`Mermaid.command(configured, default)`, whitespace-split) so a bare binary *or* an npx invocation works: defaults are `mmdc` (a binary; the user installs mermaid-cli) and **`npx -y @probelabs/maid`** (maid is normally run via npx, not a global bin ‚Äî `MermaidService.DEFAULT_MMDC`/`DEFAULT_MAID`). maid emits its JSON report on stdout regardless of exit code, so `validate` always parses it (doesn't gate on success); the real shape is `{errors:[{line,column,message,severity,code,hint}], ‚Ä¶}` ‚Äî locked in by a `MaidOutputTest` case. Settings ‚Üí **Mermaid** page: enable checkbox + `mmdc`/`maid` command fields (Browse; blank = the defaults above) + a live found/not-found status (`detect` counts any clean launch, not just exit 0). **`ui/MermaidCoordinator`** (a feature coordinator extracted from `MainController`, the `LogViewerCoordinator` pattern ‚Äî owns the `MermaidService` + the detected-tool `Availability` + the apply/gating/export logic, reaching the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface; `MainController` keeps one-line delegations and a fake `Host` makes it unit-testable, see `MermaidCoordinatorFxTest`): `applySupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`, init + every settings/theme apply) configures the fa√ßade + service + re-renders open previews, then detects the tools and gates lint/autocomplete; the `export` command no-ops when off (`ifEnabled`) and `mermaid.*` is filtered from the palette. The mermaid reads other features need are exposed as coordinator methods: `mmdcCommandOrNull()` (PDF/print embedding), `effectiveAutocomplete()` (the completion config), `exportDiagram()` (PDF diagram export), and `service()` (the Settings ‚Üí Mermaid detection-status row). **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (grammar rides the existing `opens com.editora.grammars`; mmdc/maid are external CLIs the user installs via npm). **Live linting**: `.mmd` buffers run **maid** debounced (~450 ms) while typing via `MermaidService.validate(source, cb)` (async, gen-guarded) injected into `EditorBuffer.setMermaidValidator`; `MermaidLintOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`) draws red wavy underlines at each diagnostic's `line/column/length` (visible paragraphs only, coalesced), and an `area` `MOUSE_MOVED` handler shows the maid message in a tooltip over a squiggle. Gated by `EditorBuffer.setMermaidLintEnabled` (controller sets it = mermaid on && maid detected, re-applied after the async `detect`). **Autocomplete**: `.mmd` buffers get Mermaid keyword completions (`completion/MermaidKeywords`, merged in `CompletionEngine.complete` when `snippetLang == "mermaid"`) + bundled `snippets/mermaid.json`, gated by `Settings.autocompleteMermaid` (Settings ‚Üí Editor, default on; `view.toggleAutocompleteMermaid`) ‚Äî **effective only** when the master autocomplete is on, Mermaid is enabled, and mmdc is detected (`MermaidCoordinator.effectiveAutocomplete()`; `EditorBuffer.updateCompletion` routes diagram buffers through this flag). `MaidOutput.Diagnostic` carries `length` for the underline span. *Deferred (per the SDD): a Markdown‚ÜíHTML/PDF export pipeline (none exists to hook "render before export" into), a Mermaid LSP (no LSP layer exists), and block-at-caret export from Markdown.*
- `diagram/` ‚Äî **Diagram-as-code preview** (Graphviz DOT + PlantUML; on by default, gated by `Settings.diagramSupport` ‚Äî self-gating, inert until `dot`/`plantuml` are detected). A **generic, Mermaid-independent** seam that mirrors the Mermaid pattern (`process/`+`mermaid/`) without touching its shipped path. Pure package **`com.editora.diagram`**: **`DiagramKind`** (enum DOT/PLANTUML ‚Äî each maps a buffer `languageId` ‚Üí default command + temp-source extension + a pure `args(cmd,in,out,fmt,dark)` argv builder; `fromLanguage(lang)`; a `themeSensitive` flag, false for both today so the render cache omits the theme bit ‚Üí a theme toggle is a cache hit, not a re-render), **`DiagramRenderer`** (the synchronous CLI facade ‚Äî the `mermaid/Mermaid` generalized: `renderPng`/`exportTo`/`detect`/`command`, writing the temp source to `diagram.<ext>` and reading back **whatever the tool actually produced** (`producedFile`, globbing the single-use temp dir): **PlantUML names its output after the *diagram***, so `@startuml myclassdiagram` writes `myclassdiagram.png` ‚Äî reading a fixed `diagram.<fmt>` made every *named* diagram render as "render failed" and made its export report success while writing nothing; `exportTo` moves it to the chosen dest; DOT/PlantUML both **rasterize PNG natively ‚Äî no headless browser**, unlike mmdc/D2; pure `formatFor`/args unit-tested in `DiagramRendererTest`), and **`DiagramService`** (UI fa√ßade, the `MermaidService` idiom: one `diagram-service` daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, per-kind path map + cached `Availability`(`Map<DiagramKind,Boolean>`) probe + async `export`). **`editor/DiagramImages`** is the async render engine (a near-copy of `MermaidImages`: 2-thread `diagram-render` daemon pool, LRU cache keyed by `kind+sha256((theme?)+source)`, placeholder‚Üífill; `.md-diagram`/`.diagram-placeholder`/`.diagram-error` CSS mirroring `.md-mermaid`; `configure(enabled, Map<DiagramKind,List<String>>, dark)` injected from the coordinator ‚Äî the editor package stays free of `ui`). **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the Mermaid gating: `diagramKind()`/`isRenderedDiagram()`, a broadened `hasPreview()` (`|| (isRenderedDiagram() && DiagramImages.isEnabled())`), a new `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (whole buffer ‚Üí one async image via `DiagramImages.node(kind, text, lw->lw*zoom)`, right after the Mermaid `isDiagram()` branch), and the zoom re-render. The floating 3-mode toggle attaches automatically (it keys off `hasPreview()`). **`ui/DiagramCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern, alongside `MermaidCoordinator`): `applySupport()` (init + every settings/theme apply ‚Äî configure `DiagramImages` + refresh previews + detect tools) and `export()` (active DOT/PlantUML buffer ‚Üí SVG/PNG/PDF FileChooser ‚Üí `DiagramService.export`); `MainController` keeps a `diagram` field with one-line delegations at the same sites as `mermaid` (init/settings-apply/theme-apply/dispose) + the palette gate (`Chrome.PaletteGates.diagram`, filtering `diagram.*`). **Registration:** `LanguageRegistry` (`dot`/`gv`‚Üídot, `puml`/`plantuml`/`pu`/`iuml`‚Üíplantuml), authored `grammars/dot.tmLanguage.json` (`source.dot`) + `grammars/plantuml.tmLanguage.json` (`source.plantuml`) in `GrammarRegistry` (`scopeToResource`+`mapExtensions`, riding the existing `opens com.editora.grammars`), `Commenter` (DOT `//`+`/* */`, PlantUML `'`+`/' '/`), `FoldRegions` (DOT brace folding). **Settings ‚Üí Languages & Tools ‚Üí Diagrams** page (enable checkbox + `dot`/`plantuml` path fields + a green/red found/not-found status, the Mermaid-page shape; `DiagramService` threaded into `SettingsWindow` as a ctor arg). Commands `diagram.export`, `view.toggleDiagramSupport`, `diagram.setDotCommand`, `diagram.setPlantumlCommand`; `Settings.diagramSupport`/`dotPath`/`plantumlPath` (schema 62‚Üí63 additive-identity); i18n √ó6. **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (grammars ride the existing opens; dot/plantuml are external CLIs the user installs). *Deferred: PlantUML `@start/@end` block folding, a themed (dark) render (the `themeSensitive` flag is ready), live linting (no `maid`-equivalent), the in-app installer, autocomplete, and the browser-raster diagram tools (D2, WaveDrom ‚Äî their clean raster needs a headless Chrome like mmdc).*
- `structured/` ‚Äî **Structured-data preview** (JSON/YAML/TOML tree + OpenAPI/Swagger docs; on by default, `Settings.structuredPreview`). A `.json`/`.yaml`/`.toml` buffer gets the same 3-mode preview as Markdown, via the **render-branch** model (buffer-owned, no coordinator ‚Äî like Markwhen), but hosting a **self-scrolling node** the CSV-grid way (so the `TreeView` keeps virtualization) rather than inside the preview `ScrollPane`. Pure package **`com.editora.structured`** (the only place that touches Jackson, so `editor` stays Jackson-free): **`StructuredNode`** (neutral tree: key/kind(OBJECT/ARRAY/STRING/NUMBER/BOOLEAN/NULL)/value/children), **`StructuredParser`** (`Format.forLanguage` json/yaml/toml; `parse(text,fmt)` ‚Üí a `Parsed{root, openApi, error}` via `ObjectMapper`/`YAMLMapper`/`TomlMapper` ‚Üí one `JsonNode`‚Üí`StructuredNode` conversion, capped at `MAX_NODES`=50k so a pathological doc can't build millions of FX nodes), **`OpenApiModel`** + **`OpenApiParser`** (`detect` = a textual `openapi`/`swagger` key; `parse` shallow-walks OpenAPI 3 `servers`/`components.schemas` + Swagger 2 `host`/`basePath`/`definitions` into title/servers/paths(operations‚Üíparams/responses)/schemas; `$ref`s shown by simple name via `refName`; unit-tested `StructuredParserTest`/`OpenApiParserTest`). **`editor/StructuredTree`** renders the tree as a `TreeView<StructuredNode>` (type-colored `.structured-*` cells, auto-expand depth 1); **`editor/OpenApiDoc`** renders the spec as Redoc-style API docs (title, servers, endpoints with colored `.openapi-method-*` badges + params/responses, schemas) in a self-scrolling `ScrollPane`. Both keep `editor` free of `ui`. **`EditorBuffer`**: `isStructured()`/`structuredFormat()`, `hasStructuredPreview()` (= `structuredPreviewEnabled && isStructured() && !hugeFile`) folded into `hasPreview()`, a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`, build the node on the FX thread under the `previewGen` guard into a stable `structuredContentHolder`), and the `rebuildViewHost` SPLIT/PREVIEW branches use that holder as the preview side (mirroring `hasCsvPreview()`). A **transient** tri-state `structuredShowApiDocs` (`null`=auto: API docs for a detected spec, else tree) drives `toggleStructuredView()`; default view auto-picks docs for an OpenAPI file. `setStructuredPreviewEnabled` is pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings` (like `setCsvRainbowEnabled`). **Every `set*PreviewEnabled` ends in the shared `reconcilePreviewMode()`** ‚Äî leave the preview iff `!hasPreview()`. Never re-add a per-format `isX()` test there: one setting backs several formats (XML's tree rides `structuredPreview`, yet `isStructured()` is false for XML ‚Üí the buffer was **stranded** in PREVIEW, where every `scheduleRenderPreview` branch misses and falls through to the **unconditional Markdown tail**, rendering the source as Markdown, with `hasPreview()`=false also removing the toggle needed to escape), and one file can have two previews (a workflow is YAML ‚Üí turning off structured **evicted** it from its own still-enabled preview and clobbered the per-file mode persisted in `WorkspaceState.markdownViewModes`) + `ensurePreviewControls` re-attaches the 3-mode toggle. Commands `structured.toggleView` (tree ‚áÑ API docs) + `view.toggleStructuredPreview` (the setting); Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **Structured data** checkbox; `Settings.structuredPreview` (schema 63‚Üí64 additive); i18n √ó6 (`structured.*`/`openapi.*`). **New dependency: `jackson-dataformat-yaml`** (+ transitive `org.yaml:snakeyaml` 2.4 ‚Äî **both real JPMS modules**, so they link directly under jlink with **no moditect** entry; `module-info` `requires com.fasterxml.jackson.dataformat.yaml`). **XML tree** (a 4th format, added later): `.xml` buffers (excluding `.svg`, which is an image, and `.xhtml`, which maps to `html`‚Üíbrowser) get a **faithful DOM tree** via **`structured/XmlNode`** (element/attribute/text/comment ‚Äî *not* an XML‚ÜíJSON shoehorn) + **`structured/XmlParser`** (the JDK DOM parser, **no new dependency**, XXE-hardened exactly like `maven/PomParser`; text-only elements inlined as `tag = "value"`, mixed content kept in document order, `MAX_NODES`=50k) rendered by **`editor/XmlTree`** (`.xml-*` cells). It reuses the same self-scrolling `structuredContentHolder` host and the **same `Settings.structuredPreview` gate** (not a new setting): `isXml()`/`hasXmlPreview()` + a `hasTreePreview()` (=`hasStructuredPreview() || hasXmlPreview()`) drives the shared host wiring in `hasPreview()`/`rebuildViewHost`/the mode-setter tail; a separate `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch parses off-thread ‚Üí `renderXml`. Unit-tested `XmlParserTest` (incl. an XXE-blocked case). *Deferred: GeoJSON map (an offline vector plot ‚Äî Editora ships no network tiles), specialized XML-dialect renderers (RSS/Atom feed view, like `OpenApiDoc` for JSON), jump-from-tree-node-to-source-line (needs Jackson/DOM location tracking), per-file view persistence (`WorkspaceState`), expand/collapse-all, and editing (read-only preview).*
- **SVG image preview** (`editor/SvgImages`; on by default, `Settings.svgPreview`, schema 64‚Üí65). A `.svg` file stays a normal XML **text** buffer (so it keeps XML highlighting + the lemminx LSP ‚Äî `LanguageRegistry` still maps `svg`‚Üí`xml`), but gains a rendered-image preview in the same 3-mode view as Markdown. `EditorBuffer.isSvg()` is an **extension check** (not a language change, to avoid disturbing XML LSP/folding), `hasSvgPreview()` (= `svgPreviewEnabled && isSvg() && !hugeFile`) folds into `hasPreview()`, and a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch renders it exactly like the Mermaid/diagram image branch (image node in the preview `ScrollPane`, zoom scales fit width). **`editor/SvgImages`** is the async engine ‚Äî a near-copy of `MermaidImages`/`DiagramImages` but **in-process** (no CLI/theme): a `svg-render` daemon pool + LRU cache keyed by `sha256(source)`, rasterizing via **`PreviewImageLoader.rasterizeSvg(bytes)`** (JSVG ‚Üí JavaFX `Loaded`; the same rasterizer already bundled for Markdown badge images, so **no new dependency**). `setSvgPreviewEnabled` pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings` + `ensurePreviewControls` (like the structured gate); command `view.toggleSvgPreview`; Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **SVG** checkbox; `.md-svg`/`.svg-error` CSS mirroring `.md-diagram`; i18n √ó6 (`svg.*`). `PreviewImageLoader.svgToPng`/rasterization unit-tested (`PreviewImageLoaderTest`, headless Java2D). First of the "reuse-existing-deps" preview cluster (next candidates: PDF via PDFBox, Excel/ODS via POI, XML tree, font specimen, archive contents). *Deferred: export-as-PNG from the preview, a checkerboard backdrop for transparent SVGs.*
- `cron/` + **crontab schedule preview** (`editor/CrontabPreview`; on by default, `Settings.crontabPreview`, schema 65‚Üí66). A `crontab`/`*.cron`/`*.crontab`/`cron.d/*` file (language `crontab` via `ConfigFileType`, already syntax-highlighted via the `text.crontab` grammar) gains the same 3-mode Editor/Split/Preview view as Markdown, decoding each job into plain English + the next fire times. Pure, java.base-only, unit-tested **`com.editora.cron`** package: **`CronField`** (parses one field ‚Äî `*`, `,` lists, `a-b` ranges, `*/n`/`a-b/n` steps, JAN‚ÄìDEC/SUN‚ÄìSAT names, 7=Sunday wrap ‚Äî into an expanded value set + structure for describe; range/out-of-range ‚Üí a `ParseException` with a user-facing message), **`CronExpression`** (5-field + the `@reboot @yearly @annually @monthly @weekly @daily @midnight @hourly` macros; `parse` returns a `Parsed{expr,error}` ‚Äî field-level error text, never throws ‚Äî so the preview red-flags the exact bad line; `describe()` ‚Üí English ("At 02:30, Monday through Friday", "Every 15 minutes", "At midnight"/"noon" special-cased); `nextRuns(from,n)` minute-steps forward, budgeting `MAX_SCAN_MINUTES` ‚âà 4 years **per result** (the scan counter resets after each hit) so a sparse schedule whose period exceeds 4 years ‚Äî a leap-day `0 0 29 2 *`, a yearly `0 0 1 JAN *` ‚Äî still returns all `n` runs, while an impossible spec like Feb 31 still terminates (a full scan with no hit ends the loop); it was one shared budget across all `n`, which found only the first occurrence of such a schedule (#477); **`matches`** implements the classic Vixie **day-of-month/day-of-week OR-rule** ‚Äî when *both* fields are restricted (neither literal `*`), a time fires if *either* matches. **`describe()` must gate on that same `isStar()` predicate and join the two day parts with "or"** ‚Äî it used `coversAll()` + " and ", so `0 0 13 * 5` read as "day 13 **and** Friday" (= Friday the 13th ‚Äî the very gotcha the OR-rule *is*) and `0 0 1-31 * 5` dropped the day-of-month and claimed "on Friday" while firing **daily**, all while the next-run times beside it in the preview said otherwise. Day-of-week parses over **0-7** and folds `7`‚Üí`0` only *after* a range is expanded (Vixie's order): folding first turned the canonical weekend `6-7` into `lo=6, hi=0` ‚Üí "range start after end" for a schedule real cron runs. `CronExpressionTest` pins all three, and `nextRuns` is diff-tested clean against **croniter** over 21 expressions), and **`Crontab`** (splits a file into `Assignment`s (`NAME=value`, quote-unwrapped), `Job`s (5-field or `@macro` + command, tolerant of tabs/extra whitespace), dropping comments/blanks). **`editor/CrontabPreview`** (in `editor`, no `ui` dep) renders it as a self-scrolling node (header + assignments + per-job command/English-schedule/next-runs, red row for a parse error). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the structured/SVG gates: `isCrontab()` (= `"crontab".equals(language)`), `hasCrontabPreview()` (= `crontabPreviewEnabled && isCrontab() && !hugeFile`) folded into `hasPreview()` **and `hasTreePreview()`** (so it reuses `structuredContentHolder` + `rebuildViewHost` + the mode-setter tail with zero new host plumbing), a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL` with the "now" captured on the FX thread, `previewGen`-guarded), and `setCrontabPreviewEnabled` pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings`. Snapshot **Export-to-PDF/Print** rides the existing tree-host path (`snapshotPreviewChunks` gained a crontab branch ‚Üí `CrontabPreview.content(...)` ‚Üí `snapshotNodePng`, forced light). Command `view.toggleCrontabPreview`; Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **Crontab** checkbox; `.crontab-*` CSS (AtlantaFX semantic colors, theme-tracking); i18n √ó6 (`crontab.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (rides the existing crontab grammar + the structured preview host). *Deferred: 6-field cron (seconds/year), Quartz `L`/`W`/`#` modifiers, a 24h√ó7d heat-grid view, timezone-aware next-run display.*
- `fstab/` + **fstab mount preview** (`editor/FstabPreview`; on by default, `Settings.fstabPreview`, schema 67‚Üí68). An `/etc/fstab` file (language `fstab` via `ConfigFileType`, already syntax-highlighted via the `source.fstab` grammar) gains the same 3-mode Editor/Split/Preview view, decoding each mount line into plain English ‚Äî the crontab-preview pattern applied to fstab's columns. Pure, java.base-only, unit-tested **`com.editora.fstab`** package: **`FstabEntry`** (record of the 6 columns ‚Äî spec/mountPoint/fsType/options/dump/pass ‚Äî with a nullable `error` + `isSwap()`), **`Fstab`** (`parse(text)` ‚Üí `List<FstabEntry>`, dropping comments/blanks; 4‚Äì6 whitespace columns, dump/pass default 0, `<4`/`>6`/non-numeric dump-or-pass ‚Üí an entry with an `error`), and **`FstabDescribe`** (the decode: `device(spec)` ‚Äî `UUID=`/`PARTUUID=`/`LABEL=`/`PARTLABEL=`, `//host/share`‚ÜíSMB/CIFS, `host:/export`‚ÜíNFS, `/dev/*`, and the `proc`/`sysfs`/`tmpfs`/`none` pseudo-FS keywords; `summary(entry)` ‚Äî "Mount ‚Ä¶ at ‚Ä¶ as ext4" or "Swap space on ‚Ä¶"; `options(entry)` ‚Äî a per-option dictionary mapping the boolean flags (`noatime`‚Üí"access times not updated", `nofail`‚Üí"boot continues even if the device is missing", `nosuid`/`noexec`/`nodev`/`_netdev`/`discard`/`bind`/‚Ä¶) and the `key=value` opts (`uid=`/`gid=`/`umask=`/`size=`/`errors=`/`commit=`/`compress=`/`subvol=`/`data=`), unknown tokens passing through verbatim; `checkLine(entry)` ‚Äî "fsck-checked first (root) ¬∑ not backed up"). **`editor/FstabPreview`** (in `editor`, no `ui` dep) renders a self-scrolling node (header + per-entry mount-point/summary/options/fsck-note, red row for a malformed line). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the crontab gates exactly: `isFstab()` (= `"fstab".equals(language)`), `hasFstabPreview()` folded into `hasPreview()` **and `hasTreePreview()`** (reuses `structuredContentHolder` + `rebuildViewHost`), a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`, `previewGen`-guarded), `setFstabPreviewEnabled` from `applyViewSettings`, and a `snapshotPreviewChunks` branch for snapshot Export-to-PDF/Print (forced light). Command `view.toggleFstabPreview`; Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **fstab** checkbox; `.fstab-*` CSS; i18n √ó6 (`fstab.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (rides the existing fstab grammar + the structured preview host). *Deferred: btrfs subvolume tree, per-option man-page links, a fstab-vs-currently-mounted diff.*
- `systemd/` + `sshconfig/` + `dockerfile/` ‚Äî **three more config-file previews** (`editor/SystemdPreview`/`SshConfigPreview`/`DockerfilePreview`; all on by default ‚Äî `Settings.systemdPreview`/`sshConfigPreview`/`dockerfilePreview`, one schema bump 73‚Üí74). Each decodes an already-recognized config language into plain English in the same 3-mode view, following the crontab/fstab pattern (pure package + `editor/*Preview` node into the shared self-scrolling `structuredContentHolder`; `is*()`/`has*Preview()` folded into `hasPreview()`+`hasTreePreview()`; off-thread `scheduleRenderPreview()` + `snapshotPreviewChunks()` branches; `set*PreviewEnabled` from `applyViewSettings`; `view.toggle*Preview` command + Settings ‚Üí Editor checkbox; i18n √ó6). **`com.editora.systemd`** (language `systemd`, the `.service`/`.timer`/`.socket`/‚Ä¶ extensions): **`SystemdUnit`** (INI parse ‚Üí ordered `Section`/`Directive`, keeping duplicates + `\`-continuations), **`SystemdCalendar`** (the crown jewel ‚Äî parses `OnCalendar=`: the `minutely`/`hourly`/`daily`/`weekly`/`monthly`/`yearly`/`quarterly`/`semiannually` shorthands + the general `[weekdays] [y-m-d] H:M[:S]` form with `*`/list/`a..b` range/`start/step` per field; `describe()` ‚Üí English ("At 02:30, Monday through Friday", "Daily at 02:00", "Every 15 minutes"), `nextRuns(from,n)` minute-steps bounded ~4 years, `parse` returns a field-level error not a throw), **`TimeSpan`** (systemd time spans "1h 30min"/"15min"/bare-seconds ‚Üí total seconds + English, for the `On*Sec=` monotonic timers + `RestartSec=`), and **`SystemdDescribe`** (`kind()` from the type-specific section + a per-directive `gloss()` dictionary ‚Äî ExecStart/Type/User/Restart/After/Wants/WantedBy/ListenStream/OnCalendar/On*Sec/‚Ä¶, unknown key ‚Üí null so the preview shows raw `Key=value`). The preview shows each directive's gloss above the raw line + `OnCalendar` next-runs. **`com.editora.sshconfig`** (language `ssh-config`): **`SshConfig`** (parse into a `global` block + `Host`/`Match` blocks of `Keyword value` options, `=`-or-space-separated, quote-stripped; `effective(blocks, host, key)` applies ssh's **first-obtained-value-wins** rule across the whole file ‚Äî `global` matches every host, a `Host` block matches per `SshPattern` ‚Äî and `isConcreteHost(argument)` tells a single concrete host name from a wildcard/multi-pattern line) + **`SshPattern`** (OpenSSH `Host` glob matching ‚Äî whitespace-separated patterns, `*` spans dots, `?` = one char, `!`-negation disqualifies the line, **case-sensitive**; all verified against `ssh -G`) + **`SshConfigDescribe`** (`summary(blocks, block)` ‚Üí "Connects to <HostName> on port <Port> as <User>, key <IdentityFile>, via jump host <ProxyJump>"; for a **concrete-host** block the values are *resolved across the file* so an earlier `Host *` overriding `User`/`Port` is reflected ‚Äî matching what `ssh` actually does, not the block's own line, which previously stated the opposite (#476); a wildcard/multi-pattern block describes a class of hosts, not one connection, so its own declared values are shown. Plus a per-option `gloss()` ‚Äî ForwardAgent/ProxyJump/ServerAliveInterval/‚Ä¶). **`com.editora.dockerfile`** (language `dockerfile`): **`Dockerfile`** (parse into build `Stage`s split on `FROM ‚Ä¶ AS name`, `\`-continuations, `ARG` before the first FROM = global) + **`DockerfileDescribe`** (`title(stage)` + `summaryLines(stage)` ‚Äî a curated digest: exposed ports/workdir/user/env-count/volumes/entrypoint/cmd/healthcheck/build-step-count, not a gloss of every instruction). All three reuse the existing grammars (`source.systemd`/`source.ssh-config`/`source.dockerfile`); **no new dependency / `module-info` change**. *Deferred: systemd second-granularity next-runs + `.network`/`.link` specifics, ssh `Match`/`Include` resolution, Dockerfile ARG-substitution in image names.*
- `ghactions/` + **GitHub Actions workflow preview** (`editor/GithubActionsPreview`; on by default, `Settings.githubActionsPreview`, schema 74‚Üí75). The first **content-detected YAML-dialect** preview: a workflow file stays language `yaml` (keeps YAML highlighting + the yaml LSP), but its buffer is recognized as a workflow by **content** (not path/extension) and routed to a specialized digest instead of the generic YAML tree. Pure, unit-tested **`com.editora.ghactions`**: **`GithubActions.looksLikeWorkflow(text)`** ‚Äî the sniff (a top-level `on:` **and** `jobs:` key, iterated line-by-line via `indexOf` without splitting the whole string, bounded to the first 400 lines), and **`Workflow.parse(text)`** ‚Äî reads the YAML via the existing `YAMLMapper` into a `JsonNode` (no new dep, no `module-info` opens ‚Äî like `structured/`) and walks it into a toolkit-free model: `name`, human trigger phrases from the `on:` key (**handles the YAML-1.1 `on`‚Üíboolean-`true` key gotcha** by checking both `"on"` and `"true"`; `push`/`pull_request` ‚Üí "push to main, dev"/"pull request to main" from the `branches`/`tags`/`paths` filters, `workflow_dispatch` ‚Üí "manual dispatch", `release`(types), and a **`schedule:` cron decoded via `com.editora.cron.CronExpression`** ‚Üí "on a schedule (‚Ä¶Monday through Friday)"), and each `Job` (id/name/`runs-on`/`needs`/`if`/matrix + `Step`s whose `label()` = the step name, else the short action name ‚Äî `actions/checkout@v4`‚Üí"checkout" ‚Äî else `run: <first line>`). `EditorBuffer.isGithubActions()` = `"yaml".equals(language)` + `GithubActions.looksLikeWorkflow(area.getText(0, min(len, 65536)))` (a **bounded head read**, so a large non-workflow YAML doesn't cost a full `getText()` per `hasPreview()` call); `hasGithubActionsPreview()` folded into `hasPreview()`+`hasTreePreview()`, and its `scheduleRenderPreview()`/`snapshotPreviewChunks()` branches **precede the structured (YAML tree) branch** so a workflow wins ‚Äî turning the feature off falls back to the YAML tree (`setGithubActionsPreviewEnabled` only forces the editor when `!hasPreview()`). Command `view.toggleGithubActionsPreview`; Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **GitHub Actions** checkbox; `.ghactions-*` CSS; i18n √ó6 (`ghactions.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (reuses the yaml + cron support). *Deferred: a workflow‚áÑYAML-tree toggle (like OpenAPI's tree‚áÑdocs), composite `action.yml`, and the next YAML dialects (docker-compose, Kubernetes manifests).*
- `lsp/` ‚Äî **Language Server Protocol** support (off by default, gated by `Settings.lspSupport`). **Servers: Java** (Eclipse **JDT LS**, `jdtls`), **TypeScript/JavaScript** (`typescript-language-server --stdio`, serving js/ts/jsx/tsx), **Python** (`pyright-langserver --stdio`), **XML** (`lemminx`, serving the `xml` language id ‚Äî xml/xsd/xsl/svg/fxml/pom/‚Ä¶), **JSON** (`vscode-json-language-server --stdio`), **Bash/Shell** (`bash-language-server start`, serving the `shell` language id ‚Äî sh/bash/zsh; its diagnostics come from `shellcheck` when that's on PATH), **YAML** (`yaml-language-server --stdio`), **Go** (`gopls`, root markers `go.mod`/`go.work`), **Rust** (`rust-analyzer`, root marker `Cargo.toml`), **PHP** (`phpactor language-server`, root marker `composer.json`), **Ruby** (`ruby-lsp`, root markers `Gemfile`/`.ruby-version`), **C/C++** (`clangd` ‚Äî one server serving both the `c` and `cpp` language ids, root markers `compile_commands.json`/`CMakeLists.txt`/‚Ä¶), **HTML** (`vscode-html-language-server --stdio`), **CSS** (`vscode-css-language-server --stdio`), **Kotlin** (`kotlin-language-server`), **Lua** (`lua-language-server`), **Dockerfile** (`docker-langserver --stdio`), **SQL** (`sqls`), **Terraform** (`terraform-ls serve`, root markers `.terraform`/lock file), **TOML** (`taplo lsp stdio`), and **C#** (`csharp-ls`, root markers `global.json`/`.git`) ‚Äî **twenty-one servers** total. Most already had highlighting + folding, so each was just a registry/Settings entry; the five with **no grammar** (PHP, Lua, Dockerfile, Terraform, TOML) each got a bundled `*.tmLanguage.json` (PHP `source.php` from VS Code MIT; Lua/Dockerfile/Terraform/TOML `source.lua`/`source.dockerfile`/`source.hcl.terraform`/`source.toml` from the shiki tm-grammars collection ‚Äî see NOTICE) + `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter` entries, like the JS/TS case. **Dockerfile** is matched by **filename** (extension-less `Dockerfile`/`Containerfile`, or a `Dockerfile.<tag>` suffix) via a special case in both `LanguageRegistry.forFileName` and `GrammarRegistry.scopeForFileName`; TOML moved off the borrowed INI grammar onto its own `source.toml`. **Adding a server = one `ServerDef` in `LspServerRegistry` + its id in `MainController.LSP_SERVER_IDS` + the served language id(s) in `EditorBuffer.LSP_LANGUAGES` + a Settings command/enable pair** (the Settings ‚Üí LSP page is **data-driven** over a `SettingsWindow.lspServerUis()` descriptor list, so a new server is one entry there too) ‚Äî `LspManager.configure(enabled, Map<serverId,command>)` is map-based so it never needs a signature change. The registry is **server-centric**: `LspServerRegistry` lists each server with the language ids it serves + its root markers (Java: `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/‚Ä¶; TS: `tsconfig.json`/`jsconfig.json`/`package.json`/`.git`), so `LspManager` keys **one session per `(serverId, root)`** and js/ts/jsx/tsx in one project share a single `tsserver`. Each server has its own configurable command (`Settings.javaLspCommand`/`typescriptLspCommand`; blank ‚áí default) + its own cached availability probe; `MainController` detects each independently and gates each buffer by *its* server's availability and the file's language id (`EditorBuffer.getLanguage()`, which here doubles as the LSP languageId: `java`/`javascript`/`javascriptreact`/`typescript`/`typescriptreact`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`shell`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`c`/`cpp`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`). **JS/TS also get syntax highlighting** ‚Äî bundled `typescript.tmLanguage.json` (`source.ts`) + `typescriptreact.tmLanguage.json` (`source.tsx`) grammars from VS Code (MIT, see NOTICE); `.ts/.mts/.cts/.js/.mjs/.cjs`‚Üí`source.ts`, `.tsx/.jsx`‚Üí`source.tsx` (the TS grammar tokenizes plain JS, so no separate JS grammar), with the extensions registered in `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter`. **Auto-imports**: accepting an LSP completion runs an optional `Completion.onAccept` hook (`CompletionMapper.map(items, onAcceptFor)`); for an item that `mayHaveAdditionalEdits` (carries resolve `data`), `MainController.autoImportAccept` ‚Üí `LspManager.resolveCompletion` (`completionItem/resolve`) and applies the resolved `additionalTextEdits` (e.g. a TS `import` line) via `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits(List<editor/LspTextEdit>)` (offset-mapped, applied bottom-to-top; the `LspTextEdit` record keeps `editor` lsp4j-free). Uses **LSP4J** (`org.eclipse.lsp4j` + `.jsonrpc`, automatic modules ‚Üí moditect-patched in the `dist` profile like tm4e/pdfbox; jsonrpc reuses the existing `gson`). `module-info` **`opens com.editora.lsp;`** (unqualified, **not** qualified-to-jsonrpc) because Gson reflectively reads our `@JsonNotification("language/status")` param DTO (`LanguageServerSession.LanguageStatus`) and, under `mvn javafx:run`, runs in the **unnamed** module ‚Äî a qualified opens to `org.eclipse.lsp4j.jsonrpc` alone leaves it unable to set the DTO fields accessible. **`LanguageServerSession`** runs one external server process per workspace root over stdio: it launches via `ProcessBuilder` reusing `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`/`applyStandardEnv` (the GUI-launch PATH augmentation, so a Finder-launched `.app` finds `jdtls`), drives it with an LSP4J `Launcher` on a daemon executor, implements `LanguageClient` (receives `publishDiagnostics`/log/show-message), does `initialize`/`initialized` + client capabilities, full-text document sync (`didOpen`/`didChange`/`didSave`/`didClose`), the request subset (completion/hover/definition/references), **queues requests until initialize completes**, and `shutdown`+`exit` on dispose. **The server's stderr is drained on a daemon thread** (`LanguageServerSession.drainStderr`, capped, into the Debug Log so a failed launch surfaces *why* ‚Äî missing JDK, lock, bad command) ‚Äî it **must** be consumed: leaving it a PIPE lets a chatty server (jdtls logs heavily) fill the ~64 KB OS pipe buffer and block mid-startup (LSP traffic is on stdout). (The standalone DAP adapters still `Redirect.DISCARD` their stderr instead.) **Dispose kills the whole descendant process tree** via **`process/ProcessRegistry.killTree`**, not just the launcher: jdtls (and others) is a wrapper script (Homebrew `jdtls` ‚Üí python ‚Üí java), so destroying only the wrapper **orphans the real server JVM**, which keeps running and holds its Eclipse workspace `.lock` ‚Äî the next session for the same root then can't acquire the lock and hangs (no diagnostics/completion). **Per-project jdtls workspace:** to avoid that lock contention up front, jdtls is launched with **`-data <configDir>/jdtls-workspaces/<sha256(root)>`** (`LspServerRegistry.withDataDir`/`workspaceDirName`, pure/unit-tested; base dir injected via `LspManager.setJdtlsWorkspaceBase` from `applyLspSupport`) so each root gets its own Eclipse workspace instead of the single shared default (which deadlocked when two roots ‚Äî or a leaked run, or another editor ‚Äî contended for it, leaving `initialize` unresolved ‚Üí loading bar spinning forever + dead completion). The workspace persists across sessions (jdtls's index is reused); a user-supplied `-data` in the configured command is respected (`withDataDir` no-ops then). **`com.editora.process.ProcessRegistry`** is the central lifecycle owner for *every* spawned external server (LSP **and** DAP ‚Äî `LanguageServerSession.start` and `DapClient.connectStdio`/`setAdapterProcess` call `ProcessRegistry.track(process)`): (1) **`killTree(process)`** destroys the descendant tree (children first so the wrapper can't reparent-orphan its child), then escalates to a **force-kill after a `GRACE_MS` grace period** if SIGTERM is ignored ‚Äî **non-blocking** (a daemon scheduler), so it's safe on the FX thread during a window close; (2) a **JVM shutdown hook** (`installShutdownHook`, called from `App.main`) force-kills every tracked tree on exit ‚Äî covering a normal quit *and* SIGTERM/`kill`/OS-quit/most crashes, the paths that bypass the window-close teardown and used to leak servers; (3) a small on-disk **ledger** (`<configDir>/spawned-servers.txt`, set via `setLedgerFile`) records each spawned root pid + start-time + executable, and **`reapOrphans()`** (called once from `App.start` *before* any window builds) kills any server **leaked by a previous run that died too hard for the hook** (SIGKILL / power loss). The pure `LedgerEntry` parse/format + `shouldReap(...)` decision (reap only when pid **and** start-instant **and** executable all match ‚Äî so it can never kill an unrelated reused PID) are unit-tested (`ProcessRegistryTest`). `untrack` + an `onExit` self-clean keep the live set/ledger accurate; only long-lived servers are tracked (short-lived start-then-destroy probes aren't). Uses only `java.base` ‚Äî no dependency / `module-info` change. **`LspManager`** is the UI-facing facade (mirrors `MermaidService`: one session per `(lang, root)`, cached async `detect()`, request `CompletableFuture`s marshaled to the FX thread via `Platform.runLater`, neutral `Target(file,line,char)` results, mapped-diagnostics callback, `shutdownAll`). Pure/unit-tested helpers: **`LspServerRegistry`** (language‚Üíspec + command tokenization; `java`‚Üí`jdtls`, root markers `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/‚Ä¶), **`RootResolver`** (active project ‚Üí nearest build file ‚Üí file's dir), **`LspPositions`** (offset‚ÜîLSP line/char), **`DiagnosticMapper`** (LSP `Diagnostic`‚Üí`editor/LspDiagnostic`), **`CompletionMapper`** (`CompletionItem`‚Üí`completion/Completion`; snippet-format items fall back to the label so `$0` placeholders aren't inserted). **Diagnostics UI** (`editor/`): `LspDiagnostic` (range+severity record) + `LspDiagnosticOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `MermaidLintOverlay`, multi-line/range-aware, severity colors, visible-paragraphs + coalesced, `CanvasGuards`). **Diagnostic stripes** (IntelliJ-style, fed by the same `setLspDiagnostics`, both gated on `lspActive`): the **minimap** edge stripes (`Minimap.setDiagnostics`/`setDiagnosticsEnabled` ‚Äî errors-on-top; the LSP setters only repaint stripes over an *already-cached* snapshot and **never** force a `renderContent()`/`snapshot()`, since a synchronous snapshot during the editor's first layout blanks the surface until a relayout), plus an always-on thin **`editor/DiagnosticStripe`** docked over the vertical scrollbar that maps the whole document to its height by the editor's real content metrics (`totalHeightEstimate` √∑ paragraph count, read lazily at draw time ‚Äî **no listener**, which would force eager re-computation and starve repaints) so marks sit at the actual on-screen line; mouse-transparent until it has marks, hover shows the message, click jumps via `EditorBuffer.jumpToLine`; releases its canvas to 1√ó1 when empty. `EditorBuffer` mirrors the mermaid hooks ‚Äî `setLspActive`/`setLspDiagnostics`/`setLspChangeListener` (debounced `multiPlainChanges`‚ÜídidChange)/`setLspCompletionProvider` + an `installLspHover` diagnostic tooltip ‚Äî kept decoupled (`editor` imports nothing from `lsp`; `isLspLanguage()` checks a hardcoded set of the served languages, kept in sync with `LspServerRegistry`). `ui/ProblemsPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `SearchPanel`; id `problems`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.problems`/`M-8`) groups diagnostics **by programming language ‚Üí file ‚Üí diagnostic** (language via `LanguageRegistry.forFileName`, a friendly `.problem-lang-row` header). **The active file sorts to the top** (IDE convention): `ProblemsPanel.setActiveFile(canonicalPath)` ‚Äî pushed on every tab switch via `LspCoordinator.setProblemsActiveFile` ‚Äî orders the active file's language group first and, within it, the active file first, re-sorting the cached tree without needing fresh diagnostics (pure/unit-tested `ui/ActiveFileOrder`, shared with the TODO window; the caller passes the canonical path so it matches the LSP diagnostic keys). **`MainController`** owns the manager + an `lspProblems` map **scoped to open files** ‚Äî a server publishes diagnostics project-wide (jdtls especially), so `onLspDiagnostics` drops any file without an open tab to keep the Problems window from filling with whole-workspace noise; the open-tab lookup (`tabForPath`) matches by **canonical (symlink-resolved) path** via `MainController.canonicalPath` (`Path.toRealPath`, falling back to `toAbsolutePath().normalize()`) ‚Äî a server reports diagnostics under the file's *real* URI (e.g. `/private/tmp/‚Ä¶` for a `/tmp/‚Ä¶` symlink on macOS, or any symlinked project dir) while a buffer keeps the path as opened, so plain `normalize()` matching silently **dropped every diagnostic** (no squiggles, empty Problems) ‚Äî the unit-tested fix. **The `problems` map is itself keyed by the canonical path** (`LspCoordinator.onDiagnostics`/`clearDiagnostics` run the file through `Ops.canonicalize` ‚Üí `MainController.canonicalPath`) so the server-reported key agrees with `setProblemsActiveFile` (given the canonical active path) and the tab-close clear ‚Äî otherwise the active file's group never sorted to the top of Problems for a symlinked file, since `ActiveFileOrder.isActive` compares with `normalize()`, which doesn't resolve symlinks (#470; FX-tested with a real symlink). `applyLspSupport()`/`applyLspGating()`/`ifLsp()` mirror `applyMermaidSupport` (configure ‚Üí async detect ‚Üí per-buffer `syncBufferLsp` open/activate/close), run at init + every settings apply; lifecycle: open on `addBuffer`/save-as, didChange (debounced in the buffer), didSave from `writeBuffer`, didClose on tab removal, `shutdownAll` when disabled. Commands (all `ifLsp`-gated, palette-filtered when off): `lsp.gotoDefinition` (`M-.`), `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`, ‚â•2 results ‚Üí the **References tool window**; a lone result jumps straight there), `lsp.gotoSymbol` (**Go to Symbol in Workspace** ‚Äî palette-only), `lsp.hover` (`C-c h`, hover markdown via `MarkdownRenderer` in a tooltip), `lsp.restartServers`, `lsp.formatDocument` (whole-file `textDocument/formatting`, palette-only: `LspManager.formatDocument` ‚Üí `LanguageServerSession.formatting` ‚Üí `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits` (undoable); gated by `LspManager.supportsFormatting` reading the `documentFormattingProvider` capability; `FormattingOptions` from `Settings.tabSize` + `EditorBuffer.detectInsertSpaces`), `tool.problems` (`M-8`), `view.toggleLsp`. **The entire LSP integration lives in `ui/LspCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern). It owns: the nav/format flows (`gotoDefinition`/`findReferences`/`showHover`/`formatDocument` + the hover popup); diagnostics routing (the per-open-file `problems` map + the `ProblemsPanel` + the `onDiagnostics` callback ‚Äî compact-source-noise filter + open-files scoping); and the **configure/detect/gating + per-buffer lifecycle** ‚Äî `applySupport()` (mirrors `MermaidCoordinator`; sets the jdtls workspace base, `lspManager.configure(...)`, gates the Run affordance, then per-`SERVER_IDS` detect ‚Üí `applyGating()`), the per-server `serverEnabled`/`serverCommand`/`setServer*` switches, `serverAvailable` (read by DAP's `debugEffectiveFor` via `lspCoordinator.isServerAvailable("java")`/`serverEnabled("java")`), `syncBuffer()` (open/activate/close + push trigger-chars/format/range-format/semantic flags), `updateStatusBar()` (the `LSP:` segment + Problems availability), `requestStructureSymbols()`, `requestSemanticTokens()`/`applySemanticHighlight()`, `onServerStatus()` (the ready event ‚Üí refresh capabilities + pull diagnostics + structure), `restartServers()`, `notifyDocumentSaved()`, `wireBuffer()` (the addBuffer hook set: didChange/pull-diagnostics/semantic/completion/doc-resolver/range-formatter/nav-actions + `syncBuffer`), and the `lsp.toggleServer`/`lsp.setServerCommand` pickers. It reaches the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension (open-and-goto / active-editable / lsp-feature-enabled / set-loading-bar / buffer-for-path / set-status-bar-LSP / set-problems-available / set-structure-symbols / refresh-run-button / jdtls-workspace-base / lsp-project-root). The `lsp.*` commands + `buffer.setLspNavActions` delegate to it, and the MCP bridge reads `lspCoordinator.problems()`. The `LspManager` stays owned by `MainController` (Debug layers on the jdtls session, the MCP bridge reads its diagnostics) and is passed to the coordinator as a ctor arg; its `publishDiagnostics`/`status` callbacks route through thin `MainController.onLspDiagnostics`/`onLspServerStatus` method-ref delegates (to dodge an illegal forward reference at the manager's field initializer). `MainController` keeps `lspEnabled()` (used widely by Run/Debug gating), the `ifLsp`/`toggleLsp` command glue, the Problems `ToolWindow` (built with `lspCoordinator.problemsPanel()`), and `canonicalPath`/`tabForPath`. The first three are also prepended to the **editor right-click menu** while `EditorBuffer.isLspActive()` (gated to LSP-on + a managed buffer of a served language); the menu items move the caret to the click offset first so they target the right-clicked symbol (labels reuse the `command.lsp.*` titles ‚Äî no new i18n keys). **Ctrl/Cmd-click go-to-definition:** the same `EditorBuffer` `MOUSE_PRESSED` filter that opens a Markdown link on Ctrl/Cmd-click also, in a code buffer with `isLspActive()`, moves the caret to the clicked symbol, focuses the area, and fires `lspGotoDefinitionAction` (deferred via `Platform.runLater` so focus/caret settle first) ‚Äî the IDE go-to-definition gesture, reusing the existing `gotoDefinition` flow (no new command/i18n). It only consumes the click for a served buffer, so a non-LSP file's normal click (and the multi-caret gestures) are untouched. **Format Document** joins that menu only when the server advertises formatting (`EditorBuffer.setLspFormatAvailable`, pushed from `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event like `setLspTriggerChars`). **Tab line re-indent**: in a buffer whose server advertises **range** formatting (`documentRangeFormattingProvider` via `LspManager.supportsRangeFormatting`, pushed to `EditorBuffer.setLspRangeFormatAvailable` alongside the format flag at `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event), plain Tab re-indents the current line to the server's convention ‚Äî **indentation only**, not a full line reformat. `EditorBuffer.tryLspReindentLine` (in the `addSnippetKeys` Tab branch, after snippet-prefix expansion and before `applySmartTab`) requests `textDocument/rangeFormatting` over the line via the injected `setLspRangeFormatter` (‚Üí `LspManager.rangeFormatting` ‚Üí `LanguageServerSession.rangeFormatting`), then the pure/unit-tested `editops/LineIndent.formattedIndent` computes the formatted line's leading whitespace and `applyLspLineIndent` applies only that (async, generation-guarded + line-unchanged check). It returns false (‚Üí normal smart-Tab) for a selection, a blank line (formatters strip blank-line whitespace, so a fresh line keeps the local indent), non-LSP buffers, or servers without range formatting; completion-accept / snippet-tab still take Tab first. The status bar shows an **`LSP: <server>`** segment (`StatusBar.setLsp`, `MainController.updateLspStatusBar`) for managed files, clickable ‚Üí Problems, plus an indeterminate **loading bar** while a server starts (`StatusBar.setLspLoading`) ‚Äî kept determinate (a fixed value) when idle so its animation timeline can't keep pulsing the scene and starving repaints; flipped indeterminate only during the load. The bar is **cleared when the `initialize` handshake resolves** ‚Äî `LanguageServerSession` emits a synthetic `onStatus("ServiceReady", null)` on success / `("Error", null)` on failure (null message ‚áí no echo write), which `onLspServerStatus` turns into `setLspLoading(false)`. This is **universal** across every server and a clean file that never publishes a diagnostic ‚Äî earlier the bar only stopped on incoming diagnostics or jdtls's vendor-specific `language/status`, so a no-diagnostic file (or any non-jdtls server) left it spinning forever. lsp4j's "Unsupported notification method" log noise (JDT LS's `language/status` etc.) is quieted via `App`'s `org.eclipse.lsp4j` logger set to SEVERE. **LSP completion** is an async source merged into the existing `CompletionPopup` for code buffers (`EditorBuffer.requestLspCompletion`/`mergeCompletions`, generation-guarded; LSP items first, then local snippets). **Completion fires on the server's advertised trigger characters**, not just `.`/a word prefix: `LanguageServerSession.capabilities()` carries the `initialize` result, `LspManager.triggerCharacters(file)` (pure `triggerCharsOf(ServerCapabilities)`, unit-tested) reads `completionProvider.triggerCharacters`, and `MainController` pushes the set into `EditorBuffer.setLspTriggerChars` (in `syncBufferLsp` + refreshed on the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event, since capabilities are only known post-`initialize`); `EditorBuffer.endsWithLspTrigger` checks that set. So `<` in HTML, `:` in CSS, etc. pop the completion (the trigger was previously hardcoded to `.`, so HTML/CSS completion effectively never fired even though the server returns 100+ tag/attr items ‚Äî confirmed by driving the real `vscode-html-language-server`). **Pull diagnostics** (LSP 3.17 `textDocument/diagnostic`): the client declares `DiagnosticCapabilities`, and for a server advertising a `diagnosticProvider` (vscode-html/css/json, ‚Ä¶) `LspManager.pullDiagnostics(file)` requests diagnostics and routes the report through the **same** `onDiagnostics` path as pushed `publishDiagnostics` (`DiagnosticMapper.mapReport` maps a full report, returns null for an "unchanged" report ‚Äî both unit-tested). No-op for push-only servers (jdtls/Pyright/tsserver have no `diagnosticProvider`). Pulls are debounced on the existing 300 ms didChange pulse (`EditorBuffer.setLspDiagnosticsRequester`, fired *separately* from `lspChangeListener` so a completion-keystroke flush doesn't trigger a pull) + once on save + once when the server reports ready (initial diagnostics). **Settings ‚Üí LSP** page (enable checkbox + a server-command field **per server** (all twenty-one) with Browse + a live found/not-found status row each via `LspManager.detect(serverId, ‚Ä¶)`; **data-driven** ‚Äî the page, `load()`, `refreshLspStatus()`, and `updateLspRowsEnabled()` all loop over `lspServerUis()` descriptors keyed into `lspEnableChecks`/`lspCommandFields`/`lspStatusLabels` maps, so adding a server is one descriptor; `syncLspCheck` for the palette toggle). `Settings.lspSupport` + a per-server `‚Ä¶LspCommand` + `‚Ä¶LspEnabled` pair for each of the twenty-one server ids (`java`/`typescript`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`bash`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`clangd`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`; default on, only effective under the global enable; `MainController.serverEnabled` gates `syncBufferLsp` and `applyLspSupport` calls `LspManager.shutdownServer(serverId)` for a disabled server ‚Äî **preceded by `clearDiagnosticsForServer(serverId)`** (clears every open buffer served by that id: its Problems-map entry + editor overlay, and closes the document), because *after* the shutdown `isManaged` is false so `syncBuffer`'s else-branch clear (guarded on `isManaged`) is skipped, and with no server left to re-publish an empty list the Problems window would otherwise strand that server's diagnostics forever (#469; FX-tested)). The `configure(...)`/migration maps use `Map.ofEntries` (>10 servers exceed `Map.of`'s overloads). Schema 7‚Üí8‚Üí9‚Üí10‚Üí11‚Üí12‚Üí13 (additive-identity migrations). The Settings ‚Üí LSP page's per-server **found/not-found** status is colored green/red (`settings-git-found`/`settings-git-missing`, like the Git page). Servers are **auto-detected, never bundled** (`jdtls`/`typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`lemminx`/`vscode-json-language-server`/`bash-language-server`/`yaml-language-server`/`gopls`/`rust-analyzer`/`phpactor`/`ruby-lsp`/`clangd`/`vscode-html-language-server`/`vscode-css-language-server`/`kotlin-language-server`/`lua-language-server`/`docker-langserver`/`sqls`/`terraform-ls`/`taplo`/`csharp-ls` on PATH; Settings override). **Document symbols / Structure outline**: `LanguageServerSession.documentSymbol(uri)` (`textDocument/documentSymbol`) + `LspManager.documentSymbols(file, cb)` (capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `documentSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`) map the response ‚Äî modern hierarchical `DocumentSymbol` or legacy flat `SymbolInformation` ‚Äî via `lsp/DocumentSymbolMapper` into the neutral, lsp4j-free `lsp/SymbolNode` tree (`kindName` lowercases the `SymbolKind`; `descendInto` keeps children **only for type-like containers** (class/interface/enum/struct/namespace/module/package/object); every callable (method/function/constructor) is a leaf, so a server reporting method-body internals as children ‚Äî jdtls emits locals/lambdas/anonymous-class methods, which showed as "methods inside methods" ‚Äî is flattened away. Nested functions in Python/JS therefore appear flat too). `MainController.requestStructureSymbols(buffer)` pushes it into `ui/StructurePanel.setLspSymbols(buffer, syms)` for the **active** buffer on tab switch, the debounced didChange pulse, and the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event; the panel renders an LSP-precise hierarchy with per-kind icons (`ui/StructureIcons`); method/function/constructor rows append the server's signature (`SymbolNode.detail`, e.g. `(String x) : void`) in a muted `.structure-detail` colour beside the name ‚Äî or `()` when there's no detail **and** the label doesn't already carry its own param list (jdtls names methods like `setX(Foo)`, so `StructurePanel.StructureCell.signature` suppresses the redundant `()` to avoid `setX(Foo)()`); plus a **sort** selector (Position/Name/Kind) and a **kind filter**, falling back to the fold-region/TextMate heuristic for non-LSP/remote files, LSP-off, or an empty result (`setLspSymbols(buffer, null)`). Each row also shows its **leading doc comment** as a hover tooltip via the pure/unit-tested `ui/StructureDoc.commentAbove(lines, declLine)` (Javadoc/JSDoc/PHPDoc + plain `/* */` blocks, and `//`/`#`/`--` line-comment runs above the declaration, skipping intervening annotation/decorator lines, capped) ‚Äî `StructurePanel.attachDocs` reads it from `buffer.getContent()` for both the LSP and heuristic outlines. **Go to Symbol in Workspace** (`workspace/symbol`): `LanguageServerSession.workspaceSymbol(query)` (client capability declared via `WorkspaceClientCapabilities.setSymbol`) + `LspManager.workspaceSymbols(anchorFile, query, cb)` (maps both the legacy flat `SymbolInformation` and modern `WorkspaceSymbol` shapes ‚Äî the latter's URI-only range-less location ‚Üí line 0 ‚Äî into the neutral `WorkspaceSymbolMatch{name, container, kind, file, line, character}`; capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `workspaceSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`). `LspCoordinator.gotoSymbolInWorkspace` opens **`ui/WorkspaceSymbolPopup`** ‚Äî an incremental in-scene overlay (modeled on `SearchInFilesPopup`: `OverlayHost`, `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` dismiss) whose query field re-runs `workspace/symbol` on the active file's server debounced (150 ms, stale-generation-guarded) as you type; `‚Üë‚Üì`/`C-n`/`C-p` move, Enter jumps to the symbol via `ops.openAndGoto` (cross-file), the query seeded from a single-line selection. Command `lsp.gotoSymbol` (palette-only, no keybinding); reports `status.lsp.workspaceSymbolsUnsupported` when the server lacks the capability. **References tool window**: `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`) now routes ‚â•2 results into **`ui/ReferencesPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `ProblemsPanel`; id `references`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::find`, `tool.references`, **registered default-hidden** ‚Äî the coordinator `open`s it on demand) ‚Äî a `TreeView` grouped **by file ‚Üí reference** (`line:col preview`), Enter / double-click jumps (`ReferencesPanel.Actions` ‚Üí `ops.openAndGoto`); a **lone** reference jumps straight there (no window). `LspCoordinator` owns the panel (`referencesPanel()`, like `problemsPanel()`) + `previewLine(target)` ‚Äî the one-line preview comes from the file's **open buffer** when a tab holds it (cheap, FX-safe, reflects unsaved edits), else empty (closed files show just the line number ‚Äî no disk I/O on the FX thread); the `references` window's availability is gated alongside Problems (`Ops.setProblemsAvailable`), opened via `Ops.openReferencesWindow`. *Deferred: previews for closed files (off-thread read), more languages, on-type formatting, rename/code actions/quick fixes, incremental sync, a TOML-driven server registry.*
- `run/` ‚Äî **Run a file from a gutter ‚ñ∂**, **gated by the LSP feature** (`EditorBuffer.setRunEnabled`, pushed = `Settings.lspSupport` from `MainController.applyLspSupport` on init + every settings apply; off ‚áí no gutter glyph / menu item / Run window). **Runnable files**: a **Java 25 compact source file** (JEP 512) ‚Äî detected by the pure, unit-tested **`editor/CompactSource`** (a `.java` with a `void main(` at **brace depth 0** after blanking comments/string/char/text-block literals length-preservingly; `mainLine(source)` is the glyph line) ‚Äî **any Python script** (`language == "python"`; the glyph sits on the `if __name__ == "__main__":` guard via `EditorBuffer.pythonRunLine`, else the first line) ‚Äî **or a shell script** (`language == "shell"`, glyph on line 0/the shebang) **but only when the Bash LSP server is enabled** (`EditorBuffer.setShellRunEnabled`, pushed = `lspSupport && Settings.bashLspEnabled` from `applyLspSupport`/`addBuffer`; a per-buffer gate *separate* from `setRunEnabled` so Java/Python are unaffected ‚Äî they need only the global LSP feature) ‚Äî **or a GNU Makefile** (`language == "makefile"`, `EditorBuffer.isMakefile()`): unlike the single-entry script types, **every rule target gets its own gutter ‚ñ∂** (the `.http` multi-glyph model), and clicking it runs `make -f <file> <target>` in the file's dir. The pure/unit-tested **`run/MakefileTargets.parse`** extracts each runnable target's name + 0-based line (skipping recipe lines, variable assignments `:=`/`?=`/‚Ä¶, directives, `%` pattern rules, `.PHONY`/dot targets, and `$var` names), stored as a line‚Üíname map that `recomputeRun` fills alongside the `.http` request-line set (both set `runnable=true` + `runLine=-1`); the generic **"Run File"** / `file.run` runs the **default goal** (bare `make`). `RunCoordinator.runMakeTarget(buffer, target)` saves first then streams via `RunService` (`-f <basename>` so a `build.mk`/`Makefile.inc` buffer runs *itself*, not the dir's default Makefile); `MainController` wires `setMakeRunHandler`.
