  (data-driven over `pluginManager.descriptors()`): a master *Enable plugins* checkbox + a "runs untrusted
  code, no sandbox" warning + the plugins-folder path + a **Reload** button (`discover()` + `refreshPluginList`)
  + a per-plugin enable checkbox row (writes `PluginStore.setEnabled` + `savePlugins`; load errors shown in
  red `settings-git-missing`) + a "restart to apply" note; `SettingsWindow.setPluginManager` is injected after
  construction (the page builds lazily on first `show`). Palette toggle `view.togglePlugins`
  (`togglePluginSupport` ‚Äî persists + `syncPluginsCheck`, reports a restart is needed). `module-info`
  `exports com.editora.plugin;` + `opens com.editora.plugin to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind;` (the manifest
  DTO). **Plugins load at startup only** ‚Äî enable/disable + the master gate take effect on the next launch (no
  hot classloader/UI unload; per-window `stop()` on close is the only teardown). **One new exported package; no
  new Maven dependency.** Plugin-API Javadoc (the author-facing surface) builds + doclint-validates via the `apidocs` profile: `./mvnw -Papidocs javadoc:javadoc` (scoped to `com.editora.plugin`, `doclint=all,-missing` so broken `@link`/HTML fail). Example: `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin with a
  `build.sh`) + `docs/plugins.md`. **Registry / install (browse + from-disk):** a plugin is distributed as a
  **`.zip`** whose top level is the plugin folder contents. **`RegistryIndex`/`RegistryEntry`** (lenient
  Jackson, static `parse`) model a curated **`index.json`**; **`PluginRegistry`** fetches it over HTTPS
  (the `HttpClientService` idiom ‚Äî JDK `java.net.http`, daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, HTTPS-only
  guard `isHttps`, per-URL cache); **`PluginInstaller`** (off-thread) does `installFromUrl` (download ‚Üí
  **mandatory sha-256 verify** ‚Üí unzip ‚Üí move into `<pluginsDir>/<id>/` ‚Üí `pm.discover()`) + `installFromZip`
  (no checksum ‚Äî the user picked it); **`Unzip`** is a hardened `ZipInputStream` extractor with a
  **zip-slip guard** (`safeEntryName`/`isUnderDir`) + per-entry/total/count caps. Pure helpers
  (`compareVersions`, `isSafeId`, `sha256(byte[])`, the unzip guards) are unit-tested (`RegistryIndexTest`,
  `PluginInstallerTest`). `Settings.pluginRegistryUrl` (default `DEFAULT_PLUGIN_REGISTRY` =
  `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` raw `index.json`, overridable; schema 22‚Üí23 additive). UI: a `QuickOpen<RegistryEntry>`
  browse picker (status = Installed / Update available / Install / Requires-newer via `compareVersions` +
  `AppInfo.VERSION`), an install **confirm `Alert`** (name/version/source + trust warning), a `FileChooser`
  install-from-disk, and Settings ‚Üí Plugins **Registry URL** field + **Browse / Install-from-file / per-plugin
  Remove** buttons (`SettingsWindow.setPluginActions` injected by `MainController`). Commands `plugins.browse`/
  `plugins.installFromDisk` (palette-filtered when plugins off); `MainController.onPluginInstalled` enables the
  id in `PluginStore` + `savePlugins` + `syncPluginsCheck`; `uninstallPlugin` deletes `plugins/<id>/`. **No new
  dependency** (`java.net.http` already required). **Example plugin:** the editor repo keeps a single
  in-tree reference, `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin exercising every
  extension point, with a generic `build.sh` that reads the id from `plugin.json` and emits `<id>.zip` + its
  sha) ‚Äî this is the SDK example `docs/plugins.md` walks through. **The full plugin catalog (and the live,
  signed `index.json` registry) lives in the separate `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` repo** under
  `plugins/<id>/` ‚Äî text/encode/hash/json tools, scratchpad, format-runner, regex-tester, markdown-toc,
  color-picker, word-count, calculator, run-task, slug-tools, open-on-github, box-banner, etc. They were
  *not* kept duplicated under `examples/` (that copy had already drifted); add or update a real plugin in the
  registry repo, not here.
  **Security:** consent + integrity + authenticity. (1) *Consent* ‚Äî `MainController.confirmEnablePlugin` shows a
  **capability disclosure** (jar? declared external commands + argv? keybinding remaps? via
  `pluginCapabilitySummary`) before *enabling* at every arming point (install, install-from-file, the Settings
  per-plugin checkbox). (2) *Integrity/anti-OOM* ‚Äî `PluginRegistry.readCapped` bounds the index + download
  reads; `RegistryIndex.parse` caps entry field lengths; HTTPS-only + no `https‚Üíhttp` downgrade; a
  non-default registry URL is flagged with its host. (3) *Authenticity* ‚Äî `PluginSignature` verifies a
  detached **Ed25519** signature of `index.json` (fetched from `<url>.sig`) against a **bundled public key**
  (`resources/com/editora/plugin/editora-registry.pub`; JDK `java.security`, no dependency);
  `PluginRegistry.Result.signed` carries the verdict, and `Settings.pluginRequireSignature` (default on; schema
  23‚Üí24) makes `browsePlugins` **block** an unsigned/unverified registry. The registry owner signs with
  `scripts/PluginSigningTool.java` (keygen/sign/verify, Ed25519); the private key is never committed (the
  bundled `.pub` is). Signing proves *who* published ‚Äî not a sandbox.
  *Deferred (full trust in v1, like VSCode/IntelliJ): sandboxing, hot reload, inter-plugin deps,
  GitHub-API/per-repo discovery, per-plugin/TOFU signing, auto-update, gutter-marker contributions.*
- `editorconfig/` ‚Äî **EditorConfig (`.editorconfig`) support** (on by default, gated by
  `Settings.editorConfigSupport`; schema 29‚Üí30 additive-identity). Honors `root`, `indent_style`,
  `indent_size` (incl. `tab`), `tab_width`, `end_of_line` (lf/crlf/cr), `charset`
  (utf-8/utf-8-bom/latin1/utf-16le/utf-16be), `trim_trailing_whitespace`, `insert_final_newline`, and
  `max_line_length` (incl. `off`). All **pure + unit-tested** (java.base only, no dependency/moditect):
  **`EditorConfigProperties`** (record of nullable boxed fields + `OFF` sentinel + `EMPTY` +
  `merge(lower, higher)` where higher's non-null wins), **`EditorConfigParser`**
  (`parse(text)`‚Üí`Parsed{root, List<Section{glob, Map}>}` + `toProperties` typed conversion: keys/values
  lowercased, glob keeps case, `indent_size=tab`‚Üínull, `max_line_length=off`‚ÜíOFF, lenient positive-int),
  **`EditorConfigGlob`** (`matches(glob, relPath)` glob‚Üíregex: prepends `**/` when no slash, `**/`‚Üí
  `(?:.*/)?`, `*`‚Üí`[^/]*`, `?`‚Üí`[^/]`, `[!`‚Üí`[^`, `{a,b}`‚Üíalternation, `{n1..n2}`‚Üínumeric alternation
  capped at `MAX_RANGE`), **`EditorConfigCharset`** (`charsetFor`/`writesBom`/`bomFor`/`detectByBom`
  (UTF-8 BOM, then UTF-16BE before LE)/`decode`/`encode`/`displayName`), and **`EditorConfigTransform`**
  (`transform(content, props)`: trim trailing + EOL-normalize + final-newline, idempotent, returns content
  unchanged when nothing is set so EOLs are preserved). The one impure class **`EditorConfig`** ‚Äî
  `resolveFor(Path)` walks up dirs reading `.editorconfig` (per-file **mtime cache**), matches sections,
  merges nearest-dir-wins, stops at `root=true`; `clearCache()`. **Wiring** (`MainController`):
  `applyEditorConfig(buffer)` (gated `editorConfigEnabled() && path!=null && Vfs.isLocal`) resolves the
  chain and pushes per-buffer overrides ‚Äî indent (`EditorBuffer.setIndentOverride` ‚Üí `Indenter.smartTab`/
  `enterEdit` new `(Boolean insertSpaces, Integer size)` overloads, the legacy signatures delegating
  `(null,null)` so the no-`.editorconfig` path is byte-identical) ‚Äî the **effective** indent is resolved by
  `MainController.applyEffectiveIndent(buffer, props)` with precedence **`.editorconfig` `indent_style` >
  global `Settings.indentStyle` (`detect`/`space`/`tab`, default `detect`; Settings ‚Üí Editor "Indent style"
  combo + the `editor.setIndentStyle` palette picker via `chooseSetting`; schema 30‚Üí31 additive-identity) >
  per-file `Indenter.detectUnit`** (so the global preference applies even when EditorConfig is off / a file
  is remote / has no path ‚Äî it runs in the early-return branch too; `detectUnit` reads the first indented
  line and **falls back to spaces** when the file has no indentation, matching VSCode/IntelliJ's
  "spaces unless detected as tabs" default), tab width (`setTabSize`), EOL
  (`setEolOverride`, `getLineEnding()` returns it; a manual `chooseLineEndings` change sets it so the
  user wins for the session), ruler column (`setRulerColumn`, OFF hides), charset
  (`setCharsetOverride`/`getEffectiveCharset`) ‚Äî plus `setEditorConfigProps` for save time; called from
  `applyViewSettings`. `applyEditorConfigSupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`: init + every settings
  apply; off ‚Üí clear overrides + cache). **Read/write are charset-aware**: `readWithCharset` does
  `Files.readAllBytes` ‚Üí BOM-detect ‚Üí else EditorConfig `charset` ‚Üí else UTF-8, `setDetectedCharset`,
  decode (huge-file `readCapped` stays UTF-8, documented); `saveBytes` runs `EditorConfigTransform` then
  `EditorConfigCharset.encode` (BOM-prefixed when needed) ‚Äî used by `writeBuffer` (`Files.write`) and
  `autoSaveBuffer` (snapshot bytes on FX, write off-thread); **disk-only** ‚Äî the live document/caret/undo
  are untouched. StatusBar shows the per-buffer tab size + `EditorConfigCharset.displayName(getEffectiveCharset())`,
  plus a clickable **EditorConfig** segment (`status-editorconfig`) shown only when the active buffer's resolved
  props are non-empty (`refresh()` checks `buffer.getEditorConfigProps()`, hidden in Simple mode); its click runs
  the `editorConfig.openActive` command ‚Üí `MainController.openActiveEditorConfig` ‚Üí `EditorConfig.nearestFile(path)`
  (closest `.editorconfig` walking up to `root=true`) ‚Üí `openPath`. Palette `view.toggleEditorConfig` (via the
  generic `toggleSetting`) + `editorConfig.openActive`; Settings ‚Üí Editor "Enable
  EditorConfig" checkbox (`viewCheck` + `syncAll`/`syncViewChecks`). The repo ships its own `.editorconfig` at the
  root (Java 4-space/120-col per Palantir, JSON 2-space, shell tabs, etc.). *Deferred: per-language indent
  profiles beyond the std keys, live re-resolve on `.editorconfig` edit (currently mtime-cache-invalidated),
  remote-file support.*
- `logviewer/` ‚Äî **Server log viewer** (on by default for `.log` files, gated by `Settings.logViewer`; **suppressed in Simple UI mode** via `LogViewerCoordinator.isEnabled()`). Pure, unit-tested core: **`LogLevel`** (TRACE‚Ä¶FATAL with a severity `rank()`; `fromToken` maps Logback/Log4j, `java.util.logging` FINEST‚Ä¶SEVERE, syslog, and zerolog 3-letter forms), **`LogPatterns`** (`levelOf(line)` ‚Äî an UPPERCASE level token near the line start wins, else a bracketed any-case `[error]` / a `level=‚Ä¶`/JSON field, else an Apache/Nginx access-log status 5xx‚ÜíERROR/4xx‚ÜíWARN/2xx‚ÜíINFO; deliberately prose-safe so the lowercase word "error" in a message never reclassifies a line; plus `looksLikeLog`/`hasLeadingTimestamp` content sniffs), **`LogFilter`** (`filter(text, minLevel, regex, startCarry)` keeps lines passing a level floor AND regex, where an unleveled continuation/stack-trace line **inherits the previous record's level** so an exception's whole trace survives a `WARN+` filter; `effectiveLevel`/`endCarry` make incremental appends correct), and **`LogTail`** (`readTail(file, maxBytes)` opens a huge log at its **end**, dropping the partial first line; `readAppended(file, fromOffset)` reads only the delta and holds back a trailing incomplete UTF-8 sequence ‚Äî the pure `completeEnd`/`firstLineStart` byte maths are unit-tested ‚Äî and flags `reset` when the file shrank = rotation). **`LogTailService`** (the `GitService` daemon idiom: one `ScheduledExecutorService` poll per followed file, ~500 ms, `Platform.runLater` callbacks) drives `tail -f` via `LogTail.readAppended` and returns a `Handle` to stop it. **Highlighting is two complementary layers:** a bundled `grammars/log.tmLanguage.json` (`source.log`, ext `log`) whose `markup.error/warning/info/debug/trace.log` + `constant.other.timestamp.log` scopes map (in `TextMateHighlighter.classify`) to `.text.log-*` classes (AtlantaFX semantic colors in `syntax.css`, so no per-editor-theme override) ‚Äî inline token color for logs under the 5 MB highlight cap; **plus `editor/LogHighlightOverlay`** (a coalesced, visible-lines-only `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`: a solid left-edge bar per leveled line + a faint WARN/ERROR row wash, level inheritance via a bounded upward scan, cached per line) ‚Äî **size-independent**, so the huge tail-loaded logs where TextMate is off still show levels. **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the markdown-mode bolt-on: `isLog()` (language `"log"` or forced via `setLogViewForced`), a floating `setLogControl(Node)` overlaid top-right (reusing `attachControlToCodePane`, mutually exclusive with the markdown/html controls), `setLogHighlightEnabled`, `applyLogFilter(minLevel, regex)` (keeps the full text aside in `logFullText`, shows only matching lines, re-applies incrementally on append), `appendLogText`/`resetLogContent` (follow + rotation; auto-scroll to bottom while `logFollowing`; trims past a 12 MB `LOG_FOLLOW_CAP` to bound memory). **`ui/LogControlBar`** (the floating control, the `HtmlPreviewToggle` pattern): a Follow `ToggleButton` (`Icons.arrowDown()`), a minimum-level `ComboBox`, and a regex `TextField`, reporting through callbacks to **`ui/LogViewerCoordinator`** ‚Äî the first *feature coordinator* extracted from `MainController` (it owns the tail service + the per-buffer follow/offset/control maps and reaches the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface ‚Äî settings, active/all buffers, status, `fileSize`, `requestSave`, overlay host, prompt; `MainController` supplies an anonymous `Host` adapter and keeps one-line delegations at each call site, and a fake `Host` makes the coordinator unit-testable ‚Äî see `LogViewerCoordinatorFxTest`). It owns the wiring: `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirrors `applyHtmlPreviewSupport`) (un)attaches the control + overlay on log buffers; `ensureControl` gates on `isEnabled() && isLog()`; log files **open in View mode by default** (`MainController.restoreReadOnly` adds `logViewer.isEnabled() && isLog()` ‚Äî read-only with the Enable-Editing banner, since logs are for reading and follow-tail still appends programmatically while read-only); `MainController.loadInto` opens a huge `.log` at its tail (read-only, via `logViewer.handlesLogFile`/`recordLoadOffset`) instead of the first chunk; `startFollow`/`stopFollow` manage one `LogTailService.Handle` per buffer (resume from EOF on restart so a stop/start never duplicates); `applyFilter` builds the pattern via the pure `LogFilter.compileFilter` (a **case-insensitive regex**, with a **literal-substring fallback** when the query isn't valid regex ‚Äî so a partial regex typed live, or a plain string with metacharacters, still filters), and the control's regex field filters **live** (debounced 300 ms) as well as on Enter. Commands `log.toggleFollow`/`log.viewAsLog`/`log.setLevelFilter`/`log.setRegexFilter`/`log.clearFilter` (palette-filtered when off via a new `log` field on `Chrome.PaletteGates`) + the master `view.toggleLogViewer`; `Settings.logViewer` (Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí **Logs** checkbox; schema 37‚Üí38 additive-identity). Follow/tail is **local-only** (`Vfs.isLocal`); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** *Deferred: tailing remote (SFTP) logs, a multi-file merged tail, a dedicated Logs tool window, timestamp-range filtering, jump-to-next-error navigation.*
- `i18n/` ‚Äî **UI localization**. `Messages` is a tiny static catalog loaded once by `App.start` (right after `config.load()`, before the command registry / FXML / UI are built) via `Messages.init(Messages.resolve(settings.getUiLanguage(), Messages.available().keySet(), Locale.getDefault().getLanguage()))`. Strings live in `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages.properties` (English **base/fallback**) plus `messages_<lang>.properties` overlays for **it/es/fr/pt/de**, read with `getResourceAsStream` + a UTF-8 `InputStreamReader` (the keymap/snippets loading style, so **no `module-info` opens** ‚Äî we read our own module's resources; `ResourceBundle`'s JPMS pitfalls are avoided). `tr(key)` resolves active ‚Üí English ‚Üí the key itself (a missing key is visible, never throws); `tr(key, args...)` applies `MessageFormat` (e.g. `status.saved = Saved {0}`). `resolve(pref, available, systemLang)` (pure/unit-tested) picks the explicit pref if bundled, else the system language if bundled, else `en`. Bundled languages + endonyms live in `LANGUAGES` (en‚ÜíEnglish, it‚ÜíItaliano, es‚ÜíEspa√±ol, fr‚ÜíFran√ßais, pt‚ÜíPortugu√™s, de‚ÜíDeutsch). **Command titles** come from this catalog automatically: `Command.of(id, runnable)` (the title-less overload) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id)`, so `MainController.registerCommands()` registers ids and the palette/Settings read titles fresh. **Command descriptions** work the same way: `Command.description()` (a `default` method) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id + ".desc")`, returning `""` when the key is absent (plugin/dynamic commands) so callers degrade gracefully; the command palette shows the highlighted command's description as a detail line (a `.palette-desc` `Label`) between the results list and the navigation hint, updating off the list's selection. Every `command.<id>` title has a matching `command.<id>.desc` in all six catalogs (enforced by `MessagesTest.everyCommandTitleHasAMatchingDescription`), and the website's Commands page reads the *same* `.desc` values via `website/scripts/gen-commands.py` (no separate description source). Other surfaces use explicit keys: `tooltip.*` (toolbar), `toolwindow.*` (tool-window titles), `settings.*` (the whole Settings window, incl. the language picker), `statusbar.*` (status-bar segments + tooltips), `hint.*`/`badge.*` (toolbar Switcher hint + `--dev` badge), `status.*` (the transient echo-area messages, parameterized via `MessageFormat`), `dialog.*` (every `Alert`/`TextInputDialog`/`ChoiceDialog` title/header/content + custom `ButtonType`s), `menu.*` (tab context menu), `editmenu.*` (editor right-click menu), `viewmode.*` (View-Mode banner), `find.*` (Find/Replace bar), `palette.*`/`filefinder.*`/`switcher.*` (popups), `bookmarks.*`/`project.*`/`gitpanel.*`/`branchpopup.*`/`structure.*`/`fileinfo.*` + `char.cat.*` (the tool-window panels), `markdown.*`, `autosave.*`, `branch.*`/`gitlabel.*`, `common.on`/`common.off`, `spell.lang.*`. `App.start` also calls `Locale.setDefault(...)` to the chosen language so JavaFX localizes its **own** built-in `ButtonType.OK/CANCEL/YES/NO` and locale-sensitive controls to match. The picker is a `ComboBox` at the top of Settings ‚Üí Appearance (`Settings.uiLanguage`, default `""` = Automatic); changing it saves + shows a "restart to apply" `Alert` (set-once chrome is fully relabeled on the next launch). `MessagesTest` enforces **key-parity** ‚Äî every bundled locale must have exactly the base's key set ‚Äî so translations can't drift; add a language by dropping a complete `messages_<lang>.properties` + a `LANGUAGES` entry. Essentially **all** user-facing strings are now externalized ‚Äî command palette, toolbar tooltips, tool-window titles + panel contents, Settings, status-bar segments, status/echo messages, every dialog (title/header/body/buttons), context menus, and popups. The only deliberately-untranslated tokens are technical identifiers (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, the detected language name, an example clone URL).
- **Command line** ‚Äî `App.main` intercepts `--version`/`-V` and `--help`/`-h` (print via `AppInfo` + `helpText` and exit, before `launch()`, so no GUI). `App.start` parses the rest (pure/unit-tested helpers `configDirArg`/`projectArg`/`zenFlag`/`expertFlag`/`simpleFlag`/`fileTargets`/`parseTarget`/`newFileArg`/`singleWindowArg`) and calls `MainController.startup(projectDir, List<OpenTarget>, zen, expert, newFile, simple)` instead of `openInitialBuffer()`: it activates a CLI `--project` (only if `projectsEnabled()`), restores the session, then ‚Äî via a one-shot `pendingAfterRestore` run when the deferred session restore completes ‚Äî opens any `--new-file[=name]` buffer, the `FILE[:line[:col]]` targets (additive, focused, `gotoInFile`), and toggles Zen / Expert / Simple UI mode (`--expert` mirrors `--zen`; both are per-window session state, applied after the deferred restore, and Expert wins if both are passed since the two are mutually exclusive). **`--simple`** is a *session-only* Simple-UI override (sets a transient `cliSimpleOverride`, OR'd with the saved `Settings.simpleMode` in `simpleModeActive()`); it doesn't change the saved preference, mirroring how `--zen` is session-scoped. **`--single-window[=name]`** opens exactly one window at startup instead of restoring the saved multi-window set ‚Äî the named project's window, else the no-project window (an unknown name ‚Üí no-project, with a logged warning); it's **session-only** (`WindowManager.launchSingleWindow` skips `markOpen`/`pm.save()`/the orphan-GC, and the `singleWindowSession` flag makes `reconcileOpenSet()` a no-op), so the persisted open-window layout is untouched and the next normal launch restores everything. `singleWindowArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` (bare ‚Üí no-project) / project-name, like `newFileArg`. **Welcome page**: when there are no files to restore (and no CLI `--new-file`/`FILE` target opened anything), `openInitialBuffer` no longer creates an empty Untitled buffer ‚Äî it opens the Welcome page in its own tab via `showWelcomeIfNoTabs()`‚Üí`addWelcomeTab()` (see `ui/`). `newFileArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` / name; `--new-file` ‚áí blank untitled, `--new-file=foo.md` ‚áí an unsaved buffer via `EditorBuffer.setDisplayName(name)` (tab title + extension highlighting, `path` stays null so Save prompts Save-As, the dialog's initial name defaulting to `getDisplayName()`). `AppInfo` (NAME/VERSION/HOMEPAGE/COPYRIGHT/LICENSE/buildTime) is the single source for `--version`, the About dialog, and the Welcome footer ‚Äî **`VERSION` itself derives from `pom.xml`'s `<version>`** (Maven-filtered into `build-info.properties` alongside `build.time` and read via `AppInfo.loadVersion()`, falling back to `"0.0.0"` on an unfiltered non-Maven run), so **a release bump touches only the pom**, never a hardcoded constant ‚Äî all of which show the home-page link (opened via `HostServices`), copyright, and license. `AppInfo.gitCommit()` adds the **short git commit** (read once at runtime via `git rev-parse --short HEAD`, cached, `""` when unavailable); it's shown in the About dialog and the Welcome footer **only under `--dev`** (`config.isDev() ? AppInfo.gitCommit() : ""` ‚Äî passed to `SettingsWindow.showAbout(..., commit)` and `new WelcomePane(..., devCommit)`, each rendering the `about.commit` line only when non-blank), so a dev build can tell at a glance which commit it's running. Production builds pass `""` (nothing shown). **macOS "Open With" (Finder file associations):** the packaged `Editora.app` declares `CFBundleDocumentTypes` in its Info.plist so Editora shows up in Finder's *Open With* menu for text/source files. **Wiring is macOS-only + two-part:** (1) **`scripts/aot_build.java`'s `fixMacDocumentTypes`** (run on the macOS app image before the APP_IMAGE copy / DMG wrap) writes `CFBundleDocumentTypes` via `PlistBuddy` ‚Äî a single entry declaring the **system UTIs `public.text` + `public.source-code`** (role `Editor`, `LSHandlerRank=Alternate` so it doesn't steal the default). **Deliberately NOT jpackage `--file-associations`:** that emits per-extension *custom* UTIs (`com.editora.txt`, ‚Ä¶) conforming to `public.data`, which **don't work** ‚Äî Launch Services never offers the app for a file already typed as a system UTI (a `.txt` is `public.plain-text`, which doesn't conform to `com.editora.txt`), so it wouldn't appear in Open With at all. Declaring the *system* types works because **every** text/source file's UTI **conforms to** `public.text`/`public.source-code`, making Editora an eligible alternate editor for all of them (verified via `lsregister -dump` ‚Üí `bindings: public.text, public.source-code`). (`fixMacDocumentTypes` first `Delete`s any pre-existing `UT*TypeDeclarations`/`CFBundleDocumentTypes`, tolerating absence; it's a no-op on non-mac and best-effort ‚Äî a PlistBuddy failure logs and the app still runs, just without the association.) **Two signing gotchas the plist edit exposes, both fixed in `aot_build.java`:** (a) jpackage **ad-hoc-signs** the `.app` during the app-image build, so editing `Info.plist` afterward **invalidates the code-signature seal** (the plist's hash is sealed) ‚Äî macOS then rejects the app as *tampered* (`spctl`: "invalid Info.plist ‚Ä¶ modified"; the Finder dialog says it "could not verify ‚Ä¶ free of malware" with only *Move to Trash*/*Done*, a hard block). So `fixMacDocumentTypes` **re-runs `codesign --force --deep --sign -`** on the bundle after the edit to re-seal it (arm64 needs *some* signature to run; ad-hoc is fine for a locally-built, un-notarized app). (b) The APP_IMAGE-delivery `copyRecursive` **must preserve symlinks** (`Files.isSymbolicLink` ‚Üí `createSymbolicLink`, not follow-and-copy): the jlink runtime dedups its `legal/*` license files as symlinks, and turning them into regular files breaks the seal in the *delivered* copy (`spctl`: "sealed resource ‚Ä¶ invalid: file modified: ‚Ä¶/legal/‚Ä¶"; the DMG path is unaffected ‚Äî jpackage does its own symlink-preserving copy). *(A validly ad-hoc-signed local app still shows `spctl -a -t exec: rejected` ‚Äî that only means "not notarized"; a non-quarantined local app launches fine regardless. Full **notarization** (Apple Developer ID) is the outstanding follow-up for shipping downloadable installers.)* (2) Finder delivers the opened path as an AppKit **`openFiles` Apple Event, not argv**, so the `fileTargets` argv path never sees it ‚Äî `App.start` (gated to macOS, after the windows build) calls **`MacOpenFiles.install(windows)`**, which sets a Glass `com.sun.glass.ui.Application.EventHandler` (`MacOpenFiles.Handler`) that forwards `handleOpenFilesAction` to `WindowManager.openExternalFiles(List<Path>)` ‚Üí the focused window's `MainController.openExternalFiles` (each path `openPath`-ed; a cold-launch's buffered event lands in the just-built window). `Handler` **wraps** JavaFX's own handler (delegates every other event ‚Äî quit/activate/preferences/‚Ä¶ ‚Äî to it) so Cmd-Q etc. still work; everything is `try/catch(Throwable)` so a missing internal API never breaks launch. **The handler is a standalone top-level class `com.editora.MacOpenFiles`, deliberately *not* nested in `App`:** the JavaFX launcher reflects over the `App` main class to find its methods, which eagerly loads `App`'s **nest members** ‚Äî so a `com.sun.glass.ui` subclass nested in `App` gets class-loaded (and access-checked) *before* `start()` runs, **outside** any `try/catch`, and a missing `--add-exports` there is a hard launch crash (`IllegalAccessError` in `LauncherImpl`). As a separate class it loads only inside `install()`'s guarded body, so it degrades to a logged no-op instead. The internal `com.sun.glass.ui` access needs `--add-exports javafx.graphics/com.sun.glass.ui=com.editora` in **four** places: the **compiler** args (main-compile-scoped), the **`javafx:run`** options, the **dist jpackage `<javaOptions>`**, **and the AOT-training command in `scripts/aot_build.java`** (it launches the image's own `bin/java` with a hand-built option list that must mirror the launcher, else training crashes loading `MacOpenFiles.Handler` and ships no cache). `java.awt.Desktop.setOpenFileHandler` can't be used because `App.main` forces `java.awt.headless=true` (the SVG guard). **Windows/Linux need no handler** ‚Äî their file associations pass the path as argv, already handled by `fileTargets` (associations there are an installer-time feature and aren't wired yet ‚Äî a future add). To appear, the built app must be registered with Launch Services (drag `Editora.app` to `/Applications`, or `lsregister -f`).
- `config/` ‚Äî `ConfigManager` loads/merges/saves config in the config dir, chosen by precedence **`--config-dir <path>` CLI arg (parsed by `App.configDirArg`, pure/unit-tested) > `EDITORA_CONFIG_DIR` env var > `--dev` (`~/.editora-dev/`, the `App.devFlag` flag ‚Äî a separate dev config so a development instance can't disturb production; future home for extra dev-only behavior like more logging) > `~/.editora/`** (`user.home` is the user profile on every OS); the env/default fallback is the unit-tested pure `ConfigManager.resolveConfigDir(editoraHome, userHome, dev)`. Falls back to defaults on malformed input. **Preferences** (`Settings` POJO: font, theme, keymap, tab size, view options, keybindings) are **TOML** in `settings.toml` via a Jackson `TomlMapper` (jackson-dataformat-toml). **Text zoom** is `Settings.fontZoom` (1.0 = 100%) ‚Äî a persisted Settings field deliberately *not* shown in the Settings window; `MainController.applyViewSettings` applies the effective size `round(fontSize*fontZoom)` to every buffer, `textZoom(¬±1/0)` adjusts it (status-bar `‚àí/+`, `C-=`/`C--`/`C-0`, and the scene-level `Ctrl`+mouse-wheel filter in `App`). That wheel filter routes through `MainController.zoomFromWheel`, which zooms the Markdown **preview** (`markdownZoom`) when the active buffer is in **PREVIEW** mode (`getMarkdownViewMode() == PREVIEW`) and otherwise the editor text (Editor/Split always zoom text). **Session state** (`WorkspaceState` POJO: collapsed fold regions, tool-window layout/visibility/dividers) stays **JSON** in `workspace-state.json`, and `RecentFiles` stays JSON in `recent-files.json`; `config.save()` writes both files. **Writes go off the FX thread** via `config/ConfigWriter` (one `config-writer` daemon thread): the caller serializes a consistent snapshot to bytes on the FX thread (single-threaded ‚Üí no locking) and hands the immutable bytes to the writer, which writes each file via a temp-file + atomic move (no half-written config on a crash), **coalescing per file (latest wins) and ordered through the one thread**. The frequent, coalesced in-session save (`MainController.requestSave` ‚Üí `config.saveAsync()`) is non-blocking; durable saves (`config.save()` ‚Äî used by `persistSession()` on quit, one-off actions, and `exportConfig()`) `enqueue` + `flush()` (block until written), and `App.start` registers a JVM-shutdown flush. settings.toml + workspace-state.json are the only files with both an async and a sync writer, and both funnel through the one writer queue, so a stale async write can never land after and clobber a durable one (the other stores ‚Äî `bookmarks.json`/`notes.json`/‚Ä¶ ‚Äî keep their direct synchronous `writeValue`). **Bookmarks** are deliberately *not* in `WorkspaceState` ‚Äî they're in their own `bookmarks.json` (`BookmarkStore`), written by `config.saveBookmarks()` (independent of `save()`), but **scoped per project** (bucketed by project key; `config.getBookmarks()` returns the active project's bucket). See the bookmarks paragraph in `editor/` for the per-project model and the one-time migration out of the legacy session files. Both POJOs are `@JsonIgnoreProperties(ignoreUnknown = true)`, so `save()` rewrites with only modeled fields. The switch to TOML was a clean cut ‚Äî a pre-existing `settings.json` is not migrated. (The bundled keymap `emacs.json` and the TextMate grammars stay JSON ‚Äî they're app resources, not user config.) The About dialog shows the live settings path via `ConfigManager.getSettingsFile()` ‚Äî don't hardcode it. **Export config** (owner-only ‚Äî it copies `settings.toml`'s API key + `notes.json` into `$HOME`; see `ConfigWriter.createOwnerOnly`, the single helper every config-derived file must go through ‚Äî it also backs `editora-session.log`): `ConfigManager.exportConfig()` zips the *active* config dir into a timestamped `.zip` in the user's home (`~/editora[-dev]-config-<version>-<user>-<yyyy-MM-dd_HHmmss>.zip`, embedding `AppInfo.VERSION` + `user.name`, both filename-sanitized) via the pure, unit-tested `ConfigExporter` (`zipName`/`sanitize` + `export(configDir, destDir, version, userName, now)`); surfaced as the Settings ‚Üí Advanced "Export Configuration‚Ä¶" button (wired via the `onExportConfig` `Runnable` ctor arg ‚Üí `MainController.exportConfig`, which shows the result path in a dialog) and the `config.export` command. **Projects** (`ProjectManager`, index in `projects.json`) are named single-folder workspaces; each project's session is a separate `WorkspaceState` JSON under `projects/<id>.json`. **Multi-window config split:** the config is split into a **`SharedConfig`** ‚Äî the app-wide state (the `Settings` object, the bookmark/note/breakpoint/connection stores, the user dictionary, and the `ProjectManager` index) held **by reference** across every window ‚Äî and a per-window **`ConfigManager`** that owns only that window's session (`WorkspaceState` + its `workspaceStateFile`) and delegates everything shared to `SharedConfig`. So a `config.save()` from any window writes `settings.toml` + that window's session file without clobbering another window's in-memory copy, and `config.getBookmarks()/getNotes()/getBreakpoints()` return the bucket for *this* window's project (keyed off its session file). `ConfigManager.setWorkspaceStateFile(...)` picks a window's session file (default = `workspace-state.json` for the no-project/global window). **Each project opens in its own window** (see `ui/WindowManager`); the open-window set is tracked in `ProjectManager.Index.openProjectIds` (`""` = the global window) ‚Äî `markOpen`/`markClosed`/`isOpen` ‚Äî and restored on the next launch, with `activeProjectId` as the last-focused window. `ProjectManager.Index` schema is **2** (v1‚Üív2 `ConfigMigrations.seedOpenProjectIds` seeds `openProjectIds` from the old single `activeProjectId` so a pre-multi-window install reopens its active project as a window). **Schema versioning + migrations** (`config/migration/`): every structured config file carries a per-file integer `schemaVersion` (baseline **1**; the owning POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` constant ‚Äî `Settings`/`WorkspaceState`/`BookmarkStore`/`ProjectManager.Index`, and `RecentFiles`), enumerated in `ConfigSchema` (SETTINGS/WORKSPACE/BOOKMARKS/PROJECTS/RECENT) with its current version, the version assumed when the field is absent (=1, the pre-versioning baseline), and an ordered map of `v‚Üív+1` step `Migration`s. All structured reads now go through **`ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(file, mapper, defaults, schema)`**: parse to a Jackson tree ‚Üí `upgrade` (apply the migration chain via `applySteps`, stamp `schemaVersion`) ‚Üí merge onto defaults. It's mapper-agnostic (works for TOML + JSON since `TomlMapper` yields ordinary nodes). A file **newer** than this build (`schemaVersion > current`) throws `NewerThanSupportedException` and is **backed up to `<name>.v<n>.bak`, then defaults are loaded** ‚Äî an older Editora never clobbers a newer config. `recent-files.json` was a bare JSON array (v0); the registered RECENT `0‚Üí1` step (`wrapRecentFilesArray`) wraps it into `{schemaVersion,files}` (`RecentFiles.Stored`). **To add a migration later: bump the POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` and add one `v‚Üív+1` entry to that file's `steps` map in `ConfigSchema` ‚Äî the read path, stamping, and downgrade backup are automatic.** The older one-off `migrateLegacyBookmarks()` (bookmarks flat‚Üíbucketed) stays as orthogonal field-level back-compat and runs before the versioned read.
- `ui/` ‚Äî `MainController` (+ `main.fxml`): toolbar, tabbed `EditorBuffer`s, status bar. **Multiple windows (`WindowManager`)**: each window has its own `MainController`/`Stage`/`CommandRegistry`/`KeyDispatcher` + per-window services (all already per-instance, so no static per-window state) over the shared `SharedConfig`/`KeymapManager`. **`ui/WindowManager`** (created once in `App.start`) owns the set of open windows: `buildWindow(...)` is the per-window construction extracted from `App.start`; `openOrFocus(project)` focuses an already-open project window or builds a new one; `openOrFocusGlobal()` is the no-project window; `newWindow()` always **builds** a fresh no-project window (the palette **`window.new`** command / `C-x 5 2` ‚Äî so a second window no longer requires loading a project; works regardless of the Projects feature). Each such window gets a unique **`untitled:<uuid>`** key and its **own** session file `windows/<uuid>.json` (so windows never clobber each other's open-files/layout ‚Äî they are *not* all keyed `""`), is tracked in `openProjectIds` like a project window, and is **restored on the next launch regardless of the Projects feature** ‚Äî the no-project windows (`""` + `untitled:*`) always restore; only saved *project* ids are dropped when Projects are off. `launch` dispatches a restore key by prefix (`""`‚Üíglobal/`workspace-state.json`, `untitled:`‚Üí`untitledStateFile`, else a project id) and `gcOrphanWindowSessions(toOpen)` deletes `windows/*.json` for untitled windows closed in a previous session. **Bucket:** an untitled window shares the global no-project bookmark/note bucket `""` ‚Äî its `windows/<uuid>.json` session isn't under `projects/`, and `ConfigManager.currentBookmarkKey` returns `""` for anything not directly under `projects/` (only `projects/<id>.json` gets its own bucket). `launch(...)` restores the previously-open window set on startup: with Projects **disabled** that's the global window plus any untitled "New Window"s (the default stays single-window until you open one); with Projects **enabled** it's every previously-open window. A new window is **cascaded** (offset + brought to front, un-maximized if secondary) so it doesn't stack exactly on an existing one (projects carried identical saved bounds from the single-window era). `MainController.setWindowContext(wm, project)` (called right after `init`, before `startup`) binds the window to its project ‚Äî sets the panel root/title/combo and auto-opens the Projects tool window ‚Äî so the combo shows *this* window's project (a window switcher, not an in-place swap). **Window title** (`MainController.updateWindowTitle`): the active file's home-collapsed path with a `‚Ä¢` unsaved marker, then the project, then `Editora` (e.g. `~/app/Main.java ‚Äî MyProject ‚Äî Editora`); an untitled buffer shows its display name, a non-file/Welcome tab shows just the project/app name. Refreshed on tab switch (the selection listener) and on dirty-flip / Save-As / rename (via `updateTabMeta`, guarded to the active tab). **Current-folder mode:** in the **global ("No Project") window** the Project tool window doesn't sit empty ‚Äî `MainController.updateProjectFolderView()` (called from the tab-selection listener, `setWindowContext`, and after a Save-As) roots `ProjectPanel` at the **active file's parent dir** and retitles the tool window **"Current Folder"** (`toolwindow.currentFolder`), so it tracks the focused tab like a file explorer. It no-ops when a project is open (tree stays the project root, title "Project") or while a remote folder is mounted (`activeRemoteAuthority != null` ‚Äî that root is set explicitly); an unsaved/Welcome tab (or remote file) shows the placeholder + default title. Deduped against `ProjectPanel.getRoot()` so switching files in the same folder doesn't rebuild the tree. The retitle works because `ToolWindow`'s title is now a `StringProperty` the `ToolWindowPanel` header `Label` binds to. `switchToProject`‚Üí`openOrFocus`; `closeProject` closes this window; `deleteProject` closes the project's window first; the per-window close handler persists the session, **disposes that window's services** (LSP/DAP/git/search/mermaid/pdf/print/run/autosave + buffers, in a defensive `try/catch`), and notifies `WindowManager.onWindowClosed` (no per-window "Quit?" prompt; `app.quit`/`C-x C-c`/last-window-close still `Platform.exit`). A Settings change in one window broadcasts to all via `WindowManager.broadcastSettingsApplied` ‚Üí each window's `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange`. *Window restore:* the open-window set persisted in `projects.json` (`openProjectIds`) is reconciled to the live set by a **debounced** `WindowManager.openSetReconcile` `PauseTransition` (~350 ms ‚Üí `reconcileOpenSet()`; not an eager per-close `markClosed`): a genuine single-window close (the app keeps running) outlives the debounce, which then persists the reduced live set, so the closed window is forgotten; a **quit** terminates the JVM before the timer elapses, so the reduced set is never written and the full pre-quit set stays on disk ‚áí **every** window reopens next launch. The debounce delay (rather than a plain `runLater`) is deliberate: it can't elapse inside a quit's close-handler burst, so it never persists a half-drained intermediate even if those close events interleave with the FX event queue. This covers both quit paths ‚Äî Cmd-Q / OS quit fire every window's close handler in a fast burst, and `app.quit`'s `Platform.exit` fires none at all. `reconcileOpenSet` also guards an empty live set (persist nothing). `ProjectManager.setOpenWindows(keys)` replaces the whole set (deduped, `null`‚Üí`""`). (Earlier this used a "remain" rule ‚Äî eager `markClosed` unless it was the last window ‚Äî which drained a Cmd-Q down to only the last window.) **Tab content abstraction**: a tab's `userData` is no longer always an `EditorBuffer` ‚Äî it's a `editor/TabContent` (`node()`/`title()`/`icon()`/`closeable()`; lives in `com.editora.editor` so `EditorBuffer` can implement it without the editor package depending on `ui`, the same independence the completion popup keeps). `EditorBuffer` and `WelcomePane` both implement it, so the Welcome page is a **real tab** (and future diff/image/help views can be too). **Image viewer**: `ui/ImageViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** raster-image tab ‚Äî opening a `.png`/`.jpg`/`.jpeg`/`.gif`/`.bmp` renders the picture instead of showing its binary bytes as text (the pure/unit-tested `ui/ImageFormats.isSupported(name)` gates which extensions route here; SVG is deliberately excluded ‚Äî it's editable XML). It decodes the file's bytes (`Files.readAllBytes`, so it works for local **and** remote/SFTP paths; refused above a 64 MB cap) into a JavaFX `Image`, shows a top bar with zoom out/in/fit/actual-size + a read-only badge (Ctrl+wheel zooms; fit-mode never upscales past 100%; small images center, large scroll), and `dispose()`s the decoded `Image` on tab close (releasing its Prism texture ‚Äî the per-buffer VRAM-bounding rule). `MainController.openPath` routes an image file to `openImageTab(file, select)` before the text path; `imagePaneOf(Tab)` + `tabPath(Tab)` (buffer path else image-pane path) generalize the buffer-only lookups, so image tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (restored via `openImageTab`, a `null` placeholder in the `buffers` list keeps indices aligned ‚Äî the `buffers.get(i)` reads are null-guarded) and show their path in the window title. i18n `imageviewer.*`; CSS `.image-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **Hex viewer**: `ui/HexViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** hex tab for **binary** files ‚Äî an executable/archive/`.class`/`.pdf` opens as the classic `offset | hex | ASCII` dump (pure/unit-tested `ui/HexDump.format(bytes, baseOffset)`, 16 bytes/row) instead of dumping its bytes as garbage text. **Binary detection** is by content, not extension: pure/unit-tested `ui/BinarySniff.looksBinary(sample)` (git's rule ‚Äî a NUL byte ‚áí binary ‚Äî plus a control-char density fallback, with a **BOM guard** so BOM'd UTF-16/UTF-8 text isn't misrouted, and bytes ‚â•0x80 aren't counted so UTF-8/Latin-1 prose stays text); `MainController.looksBinaryFile(path)` reads a bounded `BinarySniff.SAMPLE_BYTES` prefix. The dump sits in a read-only monospace RichTextFX `CodeArea` (selectable/copyable), reads up to `MAX_DISPLAY_BYTES` (1 MiB ‚Üí a large binary shows its first slice with a truncation note, so a multi-GB file can't exhaust memory), and `dispose()`s the text on close. `openPath` routes a binary to `openHexTab(file, select)` **after** the image check + before the text load; `hexPaneOf(Tab)` joins `imagePaneOf` in `tabPath(Tab)`, so hex tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (a `null` `buffers` placeholder, like images) and show their path in the title. Palette command **`view.openAsHex`** force-opens the active file's bytes as hex (works for a text file too). i18n `hexviewer.*`/`command.view.openAsHex`; CSS `.hex-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **PDF viewer**: `ui/PdfViewerPane implements TabContent` opens a `.pdf` in a **read-only page viewer** (rasterized via **PDFBox**, already a dependency for PDF export) instead of the hex viewer ‚Äî a top bar with `‚óÄ Page N of M ‚ñ∂` navigation + zoom (fit/actual/`Ctrl`-wheel). Pages are rasterized **one at a time, off the FX thread** on a single `pdf-render` daemon thread (PDFBox's `PDDocument` isn't thread-safe, so all document access is serialized there; only the current page's image/texture is held ‚Äî the VRAM-bounding rule). `MainController.openPath` routes `PdfViewerPane.isPdf(name)` **before** the binary/hex check; `openPdfTab`/`pdfPaneOf` + `tabPath`/`tabType` mirror the image/hex viewers so a PDF tab round-trips session restore (a `null` `buffers` placeholder keeps the fill indices aligned). The PDFBox `BufferedImage`‚ÜíFX conversion reuses the now-public `PreviewImageLoader.toFxImage` (no `javafx.swing`); works for local **and** remote (SFTP) PDFs, refused above 128 MB. `PdfViewerPane.isPdf` unit-tested (`PdfViewerPaneTest`); i18n `pdfviewer.*`; CSS `.pdf-viewer*`; **no new dependency** (PDFBox already bundled). *Deferred: continuous page scroll, a page-jump field, text selection/search, encrypted/password PDFs.* **Every** `tab.getUserData()` read goes through `bufferOf(Tab)` (returns the `EditorBuffer`, or `null` for a non-buffer tab via `instanceof` ‚Äî a raw cast would `ClassCastException` on the Welcome tab); `activeBuffer()` delegates to it. `addContentTab(TabContent, select)` is the generic tab factory (sets content/userData/close-request, appends, optionally selects+focuses) and builds a **draggable graphic header** (icon + title `Label`, `enableTabDrag`) ‚Äî so non-buffer tabs (Welcome) reorder like any other tab; the tab text is left empty, so the Switcher/pickers read the title via `TabContent.title()` (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle`). `addBuffer` calls it then overrides the header via `updateTabMeta` (drag handle, pin, dirty); buffer-only ops (pin, save, edit commands) are inert on the Welcome tab because `bufferOf`/`activeBuffer` yield null and the tab-switch consumers (status bar, Structure, File-Info, breadcrumb, git, external-change) are null-safe. **Welcome page**: `setupWelcome()` just builds the `WelcomePane` + wires its callbacks; `addWelcomeTab()` opens (or re-selects) the single Welcome tab ‚Äî held in a `Tab welcomeTab` field, cleared in its `onClosed`, with a Close-only context menu; its title (`welcome.tab`) comes from `WelcomePane.title()` ‚Äî shown in the draggable header and read by the Switcher/pickers (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle` use `TabContent.title()` for non-buffer tabs). Shown at startup with no session (`showWelcomeIfNoTabs`, run after CLI targets) and by the `view.welcome` command (`showWelcome`). Closing the last tab leaves the editor **empty** (VSCode-like ‚Äî not auto-recreated). **Buffer disposal on close**: the `tabPane.getTabs()` `ListChangeListener` (which already drops closed tabs from `mru`/`pinned`, skipping pin/drag reorders via the `reordering` guard) calls `EditorBuffer.dispose()` on each removed buffer tab ‚Äî `shutdownNow()` on the buffer's two daemon executors (`markdown-preview` + `editor-highlighter`) + `unsubscribePreview()` ‚Äî so those threads don't accumulate one pair per opened file. It runs for every real close path (close, close-others/left/right, deleted-file removal, Welcome) but never on a tab switch (selection change doesn't mutate the tabs list); the split secondary view shares the buffer's executors, so one `dispose()` covers it. `WelcomePane` reuses commands (`file.new`/`file.open`/`project.open`/`git.clone`/`palette.show` ‚Äî `project.open`/`git.clone` gated by `projectsEnabled()`/`gitEnabled()`, `palette.show` listed last) each labelled with its keybinding via a `KeymapManager.bindings()` reverse-lookup (`shortcutFor` ‚Äî Open File deliberately shows `file.find`'s `C-x C-f`) + the `RecentFiles` list (open via `openRecent`), and a footer with `AppInfo.VERSION` + a home-page link (`AppInfo.HOMEPAGE`, opened via `App`'s `HostServices` passed through `MainController.setHostServices`/`openExternalUrl`) + `AppInfo.LICENSE` (the welcome shows the license only; the author/copyright lives in About); rebuilt on each `refresh()` (also on settings apply while the Welcome tab is open, so Open-Folder/Clone track the Projects/Git toggles); styled `.welcome-*` in `app.css`. The content sits in a `ScrollPane` (`.welcome-scroll`) over a centering `StackPane` (fit-to-width, with a min width) so it stays centered but shows a vertical/horizontal scrollbar when it doesn't fit the window. **In-scene overlays (`OverlayHost`)**: the command palette and *every* keyboard picker/popup are **in-scene overlays**, **not** `javafx.stage.Popup`s ‚Äî a Popup is a separate native window that on Windows doesn't reliably take OS keyboard focus, so `input.requestFocus()` orphaned focus between the popup's scene and the main window and the keyboard went dead app-wide (mouse still worked). A single shared **`ui/OverlayHost`** (owned by `MainController`, `install(sceneRoot)`-ed into the scene-root `StackPane` from `installZenOverlay`) renders one "card" node at a time over a dim, click-to-dismiss backdrop (`.overlay-backdrop`); it owns focus capture/restore (returns typing to the editor on close), `Esc`/`C-g` dismissal, a `justHidden()` toggle guard, and `showingProperty()`. `show(content, onShown, onHidden)` centers the card near the top; `show(content, anchor, onShown, onHidden)` instead positions it just **above** an anchor node (e.g. a status-bar segment, so a dropdown "drops" from it). Each component supplies its card node (which sets `editora.ownsKeys` so its `C-n`/`C-p`/arrow nav isn't hijacked by the global dispatcher), an `onShown` hook (`input.requestFocus()`), and an `onHidden` hook (clears its own `showing` flag); `MainController.wireOverlayHost()` injects the host into all of them via `setOverlayHost(...)` (on-demand pickers ‚Äî LSP references, spell/app/editor-theme ‚Äî get it at their construction site; `MessageLogPopup` via `StatusBar.setOverlayHost`). Converted: `CommandPalette` (M-x; the footer legend lists `esc`/`C-g`, no separator above it), the generic `QuickOpen<T>` pickers (recent files, structure, open files, tool windows, bookmarks, notes/notes-search, snippets, projects, LSP references, themes), `FileFinder` (file + folder finders), `Switcher` (IntelliJ Ctrl-Tab), the Git `BranchPopup` (anchored), and `MessageLogPopup` (anchored). When a card is anchored to a status-bar segment, the full-scene backdrop intercepts a re-click on that segment (closes the overlay, doesn't reach the segment) ‚Äî a clean click-to-toggle. (`editor/CompletionPopup` stays a `Popup` ‚Äî it never calls `requestFocus()`, so it's safe.) `FindReplaceBar` (find/replace with case + regex) was already in-scene the same way. **Input dialogs** are also in-scene via **`ui/OverlayInput`** ‚Äî a stateless helper that builds a form card (title + caller-supplied body + footer Cancel/OK, optional left-aligned Delete `Extra`, optional `okEnabled` validity gate) and shows it through the same `OverlayHost`; the card sets `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` cancel (host), and `Enter` accepts (or `Ctrl/Cmd+Enter` when `ctrlEnterToSubmit` for the multi-line note editor). `onAccept` runs **after** the card hides (focus already back in the editor) ‚Äî flows are callback-driven, no blocking `showAndWait`. `MainController.promptText(title,label,initial,onAccept)` is the single-line convenience (installs `TextInputKeymap` for Emacs caret nav) and doubles as the `OverlayInput.Prompt` functional interface injected into `BookmarksPanel`/`ProjectPanel` (`setPrompt`) so those tool windows prompt without needing the host/keymap. Converted off native `TextInputDialog`/`Dialog`: the Personal Note editor (`showNoteDialog`, multi-line + Delete), bookmark-note edit, file rename (tab + project tree), Git **clone** (two fields + Browse + validity gate) and **new branch**, **go to line**, and **Save As from the command palette / a keybinding** (`saveAsPrompt` ‚Äî a path prompt pre-filled with the current path, or the project folder + suggested name for an untitled buffer; a bare name resolves against that folder and `~` expands, via the pure/unit-tested `config/PathKeys.resolveUserInput`; overwriting a different existing file still uses a native confirm `Alert`). The **toolbar Save-As button keeps the native `FileChooser`** (its FXML `onAction="#onSaveAs"`, a mouse action) ‚Äî only the `file.saveAs` command routes to the in-scene prompt, so keyboard = prompt, mouse = chooser. Deliberately left **native**: simple `Alert` confirmations (overwrite/delete/external-change) and the `ChoiceDialog` selectors (set language / tab size / line endings) + the `i18n` key `dialog.ok`. **Status-bar message log**: every echo-area message set via `MainController.setStatus`‚Üí`StatusBar.setMessage` is recorded (non-blank only) in an in-memory, **session-only** `MessageLog` (pure model, capped at `MAX_ENTRIES`=200, oldest evicted, newest-first `entries()`; unit-tested). The echo label is clickable (`view.messageLog` command) ‚Üí `StatusBar.showMessageLog()` ‚Üí `MessageLogPopup.toggle` (a second click on the echo **closes** it ‚Äî the backdrop intercepts it; a `lastHiddenAt` guard absorbs the close-then-click race) ‚Üí a `MessageLogPopup` (an `OverlayHost`-anchored scrollable `ListView` above the echo; each row an `HH:mm:ss` time indicator + the message; long messages **wrap** (the row grows in height ‚Äî no horizontal scrollbar, the row width is bound to the list viewport). Rows are **multi-selectable**; a footer **Copy** button copies the selected messages (or all when none are selected, joined by newline ‚Äî `‚åò/Ctrl+C` also works) and a **Clear** action empties the log; Esc / `C-g` / `M-g` close it. (The popup is sized 552√ó280 ‚Äî 20% wider than the original ‚Äî and has no per-row right-click menu; the Copy button replaced it for discoverability.) Not persisted. Styled `.message-log*` in `app.css`. **Debug Log** (distinct from the echo MessageLog): `ui/DebugLog` is a static capture of the app's **`java.util.logging`** output + **uncaught exceptions** ‚Äî installed in `App.main` (`DebugLog.install()`: a root-logger `Handler` at `Level.ALL` appending to a bounded ring buffer + `Thread.setDefaultUncaughtExceptionHandler`) so a packaged build (DMG/MSI/DEB, no visible stderr) can still surface errors; `App.start` calls `DebugLog.attachFile(config.getConfigDir())` to also mirror records to `editora-session.log` (truncated per session) so they survive a crash for a bug report. `ui/DebugLogWindow` shows the buffer in a read-only monospace `TextArea` (Refresh/Copy/Clear/Export‚Ä¶), opened by the `view.debugLog` command and the **Settings ‚Üí Advanced ‚Üí "Show Debug Log‚Ä¶"** button (wired via the `onShowDebugLog` `Runnable` ctor arg ‚Üí `MainController.showDebugLog`). Pure helpers (`shortName`, the bounded `append`, `format`) are unit-tested. **Unsaved-file indicator consistency**: every surface that lists open buffers shows the same dirty marker as the tab strip (a `‚Ä¢ ` prefix + amber-italic `.dirty-name` in `app.css`): the **Switcher** (its cell checks `buffer.isDirty()`), the **Open Files** picker (`buffer.jump` ‚Äî its label adds the `‚Ä¢ ` and `QuickOpen.setItemStyleClass(tab -> isTabDirty(tab) ? "dirty-name" : null)` colors it; the `searchKey` stays the plain name), and the **Project tool window** tree (the pre-existing `.modified-file` cell class, refreshed via `projectPanel.refreshModified()` on every dirty-flag change). **Git file coloring (IntelliJ-style):** the Project tree colors each file by its Git working-tree status ‚Äî added = green, modified = blue, deleted = gray, renamed = violet, untracked = olive, and a folder containing changed descendants is tinted blue. The pure/unit-tested **`git/GitFileStatus`** enum (`of(FileEntry)` classifies porcelain-v2 index/worktree letters ‚Äî deleted‚Üírenamed‚Üíadded‚Üímodified precedence, untracked first; `byPath(GitStatus, root)` ‚Üí `Map<Path, GitFileStatus>` keyed by absolute-normalized path) drives it; `GitCoordinator.applyState` pushes the map (or empty on non-repo / Git-off) via `Ops.setProjectGitStatus` ‚Üí `MainController` ‚Üí `ProjectPanel.setGitStatus`, which stores it + derives the set of changed ancestor dirs and `tree.refresh()`es. The `PathCell` adds the status's `.git-status-*` class (or `.git-status-dir-changed` on a folder) ‚Äî but an **unsaved (`.modified-file`) file keeps its amber marker, which takes precedence**. Colors ride the Git feature (updated on the same tab-switch / focus / save / mutation cadence as the gutter change bars); no separate setting/command. CSS `.project-tree .git-status-*` (+ `.git-tree .git-status-*`) in `app.css` (semantic `-color-accent-fg`/`-color-success-fg` + fixed olive/violet). Each changed file also shows a **single-letter status prefix** (`GitFileStatus.letter()` ‚Üí M/A/D/R/U) matching the Commit tool window, and the **Commit window's rows are colored by the same `.git-status-*` classes** (`GitPanel.GitCell` adds `GitFileStatus.of(entry).cssClass()`), so the two panels read identically; an unsaved-in-editor file keeps its amber `‚Ä¢` instead of a Git letter. **Project-tree Git actions** (the cell right-click **Git** submenu, `ProjectPanel.FileActions`): files offer **Stage** / **Unstage** / **Revert‚Ä¶** / **Add to .gitignore** + **Compare with HEAD** / **Compare with Branch‚Ä¶** / **Compare with Revision‚Ä¶** / **Annotate** / **Show File History**; folders offer **Stage** / **Revert‚Ä¶** of the whole subtree. The path-based ops live in `GitCoordinator` (`gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`, all repo-relative via `rel(...)` and refreshing through `afterMutation()`): Revert reuses the confirming `discardChanges` (untracked ‚Üí `git clean`, else `git checkout`, deciding via the stored `lastStatusByPath`); Add-to-.gitignore appends the pure/unit-tested `git/GitIgnore.entryFor`/`withEntry` line to the repo-root `.gitignore`. The three navigation/inspection actions delegate to path-based entry points: **Compare with Branch** ‚Üí `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsBranch(path)` (a `QuickOpen<String>` over `GitService.branches` local+remote, diffing working ‚Üî `<branch>:rel`), **Compare with Revision** ‚Üí `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsCommit(path)` (the path-based extraction of `diffActiveVsCommit`, a commit picker over the file's log ‚Äî `diffActiveVsCommit` now delegates to it), and **Annotate** ‚Üí open the file + `GitCoordinator.annotateActive()` (enables inline blame if off, then `applyBlame`). The menu items enable/disable off `ProjectPanel`'s own `gitStatus`/`gitChangedDirs` (Revert only when the file/folder has changes; Add-to-.gitignore only for untracked), and the whole Git submenu greys out with no VCS (`FileActions.gitAvailable`). **The editor tab's right-click menu mirrors this same Git submenu** (`MainController.installTabMenu`), acting on *that tab's* file (`buffer.getPath()`) via the same path-based ops (`GitCoordinator.gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`/`annotateActive`, `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVs{Head,Branch,Commit}`, `gitFileHistoryForPath`) and the same `project.menu.git.*` labels; `GitCoordinator.statusFor(path)` gates **Revert** (only when the file has changes) / **Add to .gitignore** (untracked only), the submenu is hidden for an untitled buffer and greyed out with no VCS. The pre-existing tab **"Compare With‚Ä¶"** (any two files) + **"Open in Diff Viewer"** (`.patch`/`.diff`) stay *outside* the submenu ‚Äî they aren't Git ops. **Project tree filesystem refresh**: `ProjectPanel.refreshTree()` re-scans the tree against disk (files/folders added/removed outside Editora) while **preserving the expanded folders + selection** (it collects expanded paths, `reload()`s only the expanded directories, re-expands by path, restores the selection) ‚Äî no-op while filtering/no project; called on window focus-regain (alongside `checkExternalChanges`/`refreshGit`) **and by a filesystem watcher**. **Live filesystem watcher**: `ProjectPanel` runs a `java.nio.file.WatchService` (daemon `project-fs-watch` thread) over the **root + currently-expanded directories** (re-synced via `syncWatches()` on expand/collapse and after each rebuild ‚Äî cheap even on huge trees; a collapsed folder isn't watched since it isn't visible, and expanding re-lists it). Disk events (create/delete/modify) are drained and coalesced by a 250 ms `PauseTransition` into a single `refreshTree()`. **Local roots only** (`Vfs.isLocal`; a remote SFTP root has no local watcher). Lifecycle: started in `setRoot` (`ensureWatchOrStop`), torn down in `ProjectPanel.dispose()` (closes the service + thread), called from `MainController.disposeWindow`. *(On macOS the JDK's WatchService is a poller, so external changes can lag a few seconds ‚Äî the focus-regain refresh covers the immediate case.)* In-app rename/delete update the tree instantly via `refreshAfterChange()` ‚Üí `refreshTree()` (re-list from disk **by path**, not the captured `TreeItem` ‚Äî the confirm/rename dialog is a separate window, so closing it regains focus on the main window and fires the focus-regain `refreshTree()` which rebuilds the nodes, detaching the captured item; re-listing by path is immune to that) and call `markLocalChange()` so the watcher **skips its redundant ~1s-later refresh** for the app's own change (a `SELF_CHANGE_WINDOW_MS` guard in the debounce handler). **Mini file manager:** the tree is `SelectionMode.MULTIPLE` (arrow-key nav uses `clearAndSelect`, so it stays single; mouse Ctrl/Cmd- + Shift-click multi-selects), and each `PathCell` has drag handlers to **move** a file/folder (or the whole multi-selection ‚Äî `actionTargets`) onto a **folder** cell (or the root): `setOnDragDetected` stores the paths in `draggedPaths` + a snapshot drag view, `setOnDragOver` accepts `MOVE` + adds `.project-drop-target` when `canDropInto` (a folder cell only, via `dropTargetDir`), and `setOnDragDropped` runs `moveInto(sources, targetDir)` ‚Äî `Files.move` per source, skipping no-ops/conflicts/invalid moves (the pure, unit-tested `canMoveInto`: not the current parent, not into its own subtree), then `onFileRenamed.accept(src, dest)` per moved path. **Right-click Delete acts on the whole multi-file selection** (`deleteSelected` ‚Üí `actionTargets`, one confirm; files only). `MainController.onProjectFileRenamed` was widened to **prefix-remap** every open buffer under a moved directory (not just an exact-path file match), so a moved folder's open tabs follow to the new path; a `setOnStatus(this::setStatus)` sink shows the move/delete feedback. **External change detection**: each buffer records its file's on-disk mtime+size at load/save (`EditorBuffer.setDiskSnapshot`/`diskChangedFrom`); `MainController.checkExternalChanges()` checks the **active tab's** file and, if its disk stamp changed under it, prompts (`promptExternalChange` ‚Üí `reloadFromDisk`). It runs on window focus-regain (`stage.focusedProperty`) and on tab switch ‚Äî so the prompt only appears for the file the user is looking at; background tabs are checked when switched to. A re-entrancy guard stops the modal prompt from re-triggering itself; "Keep" re-baselines the snapshot; deleted files are skipped; the app's own writes re-baseline so they never prompt. **`SettingsWindow`** is a scalable shell: a top search box + a left **grouped** sidebar + a per-category page (built once into a `Map<Category,Region>`), with a bottom **Reset to Defaults** + Close. The sidebar is a `ListView<Object>` of mixed rows ‚Äî a non-selectable **`Group`** header (muted, `.settings-group-header`, mouse-transparent) followed by its indented **`Category`** items (`.settings-sidebar-item`), built by `sidebarItems()` in `Category` declaration order; the selection listener swaps the page only for an `instanceof Category` row. **Five groups** (`Group` enum, in order): **General** (Appearance / Interface / Workspace / Tool Windows), **Editor** (Editor = General display+indent+saving+logs+PDF / Code Completion / Snippets / Templates / TODO / Spell Check / Search), **Languages & Tools** (Language Servers / Debugger / Markdown / Mermaid / Web / External Tools), **Version Control** (Git), **System** (Keymap / Remote / Plugins / MCP / Advanced). This replaced the old flat 22-entry list: the catch-all *Editor* page was split (**Code Completion** + **TODO** are now their own leaves), the *Application* grab-bag dissolved into **Interface** (chrome: toolbar/status-bar/tab-bar/breadcrumb/tool-stripe + Simple/Zen/Expert **Modes**) + **Workspace** (Projects / show-hidden-files / Notes / Local History), the author field moved to **Templates**, and the two one-toggle *HTTP Client* + *HTML Preview* pages merged into **Web** (two sections). Each feature's master toggle now lives on one canonical page (the Tool Windows page's gated-window notes point there); the AI category grew from a "coming soon" placeholder into three real pages ‚Äî **AI** / **Agent** / inline completion, see the `ai/`+`agent/` bullet (no more `placeholder` flag / `placeholderPage`). `filter()` greys non-matching categories **and** empty group headers (`searchHiddenCats` + `searchHiddenGroups`) and auto-selects the first hit. New i18n: `settings.group.*` + `settings.cat.interface/workspace/completion/todo/web` + `settings.section.modes/htmlPreview/httpClient/templatesList`. The **Snippets** + **Templates** body fields are now RichTextFX `CodeArea`s (not `TextArea`s) with live TextMate highlighting for the snippet/template language (`highlightSnippetBody` via `GrammarRegistry`+`TextMateHighlighter`, re-run on edit) + basic Emacs caret movement (`installEmacsKeys`: `C-a/C-e/C-f/C-b/C-n/C-p/M-f/M-b/C-d/C-k`, since the settings scene has no global `KeyDispatcher`). `formRow` pins each label's min width to its preferred width so a tight `GridPane` never collapses labels to "‚Ä¶". It keeps the **live-apply** model (each control writes its `Settings` field then `apply()` ‚Üí `config.save()` + `onApply`); there is no OK/Cancel. **Search** filters via the pure/unit-tested `SettingsWindow.matches(query, keywords)` (hides non-matching rows + empty section headers, disables sidebar categories with no hits, auto-selects the first match). The **Appearance** page has a **live preview**: a read-only `CodeArea` (`editor-area`) highlighted once via `TextMateHighlighter.compute(sample, java grammar)`; the Settings `Scene` carries `app.css`+`syntax.css` and an editor-theme override sheet swapped on theme change (mirroring `MainController.applyEditorTheme`), so the preview recolors for free; font changes update its inline style. **Reset** (a single "Reset to Defaults" on the Advanced page) ‚Üí **`Settings.resetToDefaults(live)`**, which copies every property Jackson persists off a fresh `new Settings()` onto the live instance **in place** (every window holds that reference), preserving only `fontZoom` + `keybindings`. **Never replace it with a list of setters** ‚Äî that is what it was, and the list rotted to **23 of 181 fields**, so Reset silently left ~87% of preferences (all of AI/LSP/Debug/previews/build-tools/`simpleMode`/`keymap`/`uiLanguage`, and the `aiApiKey`) untouched; driving it off the serialized form covers a new setting the day it is added. **Tool stripe toggle**: the **Interface** page has a "Show tool stripe" checkbox (`Settings.showToolStripe`, default on, schema bumped 3‚Üí4 additive-identity) at the top with a `note(...)` warning that hiding the stripe **takes precedence** over each tool window's individual visibility toggle below. It's UI-only ‚Äî `ToolWindowManager.setStripesEnabled(false)` hides the left/right/bottom stripe `Pane`s (folded into `setStripeShown`'s `stripesEnabled && !zenHidesStripes && !empty` guard) but tool windows still open via their keys (`M-1`‚Ä¶) and the palette. `MainController.applyChromeVisibility()` calls `toolWindows.setStripesEnabled(s.isShowToolStripe())` (re-applied on every settings apply + at init); the palette command `view.toggleToolStripe` (`MainController.toggleToolStripe`) flips the setting, saves, re-applies, and re-syncs the checkbox via `SettingsWindow.syncToolStripeCheck()`. **Simple UI mode** (`Settings.simpleMode`, default off, schema 19‚Üí20 additive-identity; Settings ‚Üí Interface "Simple UI mode", a toolbar `Icons.simpleMode()` square button + `onToggleSimpleMode`, palette `view.toggleSimpleMode`, and the `--simple` CLI session-override) is a single toggle that strips chrome to a minimal surface. `applyChromeVisibility` calls **`applySimpleMode()`** (the effective state is `simpleModeActive()` = `Settings.simpleMode || cliSimpleOverride`): it hides a curated set of toolbar buttons (`newFromTemplateButton`/`recentButton`/`clearRecentButton`/`findInFilesButton`/`splitVertical`/`splitHorizontal` ‚Äî the **Open** button is deliberately kept so opening a file stays one click away) then **collapses orphaned separators** via `collapseToolbarSeparators()` (a generic pass hiding any `Separator` with no visible control before+after ‚Äî self-correcting, so toggling off restores them), and pushes `statusBar.setSimpleMode(...)` (hides the git/language/tab-size/line-ending/encoding segments **and the LSP server segment + loading bar** ‚Äî the LSP ones are event-driven, so `setLsp`/`setLspLoading` store their state and route through `applyLspStatusVisibility()` which suppresses them while `simpleMode`; keeps echo/read-only/zoom/Ln-Col **and the file size**). The **tool-window stripe** and **breadcrumb** are hidden via effective values right in `applyChromeVisibility` (`setStripesEnabled(showToolStripe && !simple)`, `breadcrumb.setEnabled(showBreadcrumb && !simple)`). The project toolbar group is gated inside `applyProjectSupport` (`on && !simpleModeActive()`, since it runs after `applyChromeVisibility`). The minimap is hidden via an **effective value in `applyViewSettings`** (`buffer.setMinimapVisible(showMinimap && !simpleModeActive())`) so the saved pref is preserved; the **whole gutter** is removed via `buffer.setGutterVisible(!simpleModeActive())` (a flag making `refreshGutter()` set a **null `setParagraphGraphicFactory`** ‚Äî no line numbers, fold chevrons, or bookmark/note/run/breakpoint/git slots), and when Simple mode is active `applyViewSettings` also calls `buffer.unfoldAll()` so collapsed regions aren't stranded behind the hidden chevrons. (`setLineNumbersVisible` is still applied for the non-simple state.) `toggleSimpleMode()` mirrors `toggleToolStripe` (clears `cliSimpleOverride`, flips + saves, `applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`, `syncSimpleModeCheck`, localized `status.toggle.simpleMode` echo) and, when **entering** Simple mode, **closes any open tool window** (`toolWindows.getOpenToolWindows()` ‚Üí `close`) since the stripe is hidden. (Toolbar layout: the **Settings** button sits just left of **About**, each set off by a small `Separator` ‚Äî a general arrangement, not Simple-mode-specific.) Simple mode also **disables the heavier features**: `lspEnabled()`, `debugSupportEnabled()`, `httpEnabled()`, `gitEnabled()`, and `multiCaretEnabled()` each fold in `&& !simpleModeActive()`, and their `apply*` methods compute `on` from those helpers ‚Äî so toggling Simple mode on shuts down language servers + debug adapters, gates off the HTTP ‚ñ∂, disables the Git integration (status-bar VCS segment, gutter change bars, Commit window), and turns off **multiple cursors / Alt+drag column selection** (`applyMultiCaret` pushes the effective off to every buffer; `withMultiCaret` reports "disabled") ‚Äî all reusing each feature's existing enable‚Üídisable path, and toggling off restores them from the untouched saved settings. The `git.*`/`lsp.*`/`http.*` palette commands (and the Commit/Problems/HTTP tool-window picker entries) are filtered out via those same effective gates while Simple mode is on. Tabs stay; the `--dev` badge stays (a deliberate dev indicator). **About** is no longer in Settings (it's on the toolbar + `help.about`; `SettingsWindow.showAbout` is still the shared dialog); the settings-file link moved to the **Advanced** page. Keep its public API (`show`/`syncThemes`/`syncProjectsCheck`/`syncToolStripeCheck`/`showAbout`/`displaySettingsPath`) ‚Äî `MainController` wiring is unchanged.

## Conventions

- **Performance is a top priority.** Editora must stay fast and responsive, especially on large files. Treat the UI thread as sacred and these as the hot paths: typing/editing, scrolling, syntax highlighting, the document overlays (whitespace, minimap, 80-column ruler), and the line-number gutter. Rules to uphold:
  - **Never block the JavaFX Application Thread** with non-trivial work ‚Äî tokenize/parse/search off-thread (see the `highlightExecutor` pattern in `EditorBuffer`) and apply results back on the FX thread with a generation/stale-result guard.
  - **Debounce and coalesce** ‚Äî re-highlighting is debounced; overlay/ruler/minimap redraws coalesce to one per pulse (a `pending` flag + `Platform.runLater`). Don't add per-keystroke or per-scroll-pulse work that isn't coalesced.
  - **Work incrementally / only on what's visible** ‚Äî highlighting re-tokenizes only from the changed line; overlays iterate just the visible paragraphs (`firstVisibleParToAllParIndex ‚Ä¶ last`) and skip folded lines. Avoid O(document) work on edits or scrolls.
  - **Don't defeat the per-node CSS style cache** ‚Äî keep token rules as the compound `.text.<class>` selector (see `syntax.css`); coalesce adjacent same-style spans (`SpanMerger`) before `setStyleSpans`; never query `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen` synchronously inside a layout/viewport event.
  - **Large/huge files** already disable highlighting + minimap (‚â•5 MB) and go read-only with a capped load (‚â•50 MB); preserve those guards. There's also an **intermediate large-source tier** (`EditorBuffer.heavyFile` / `setHeavyFile` / `isHeavyFile`, set in `MainController.loadInto` when a sub-5 MB file's `lineCount()` ‚â• `Settings.largeFileThreshold`, default 10000 lines, 0 = off): it **disables the minimap + LSP** (the two heaviest features for a very long single source) but **keeps syntax highlighting + editing**; `largeFile` implies the same minimap/LSP suppression. Per-buffer toggleable (`view.toggleLargeFileMode` ‚Üí `MainController.toggleLargeFileMode`, which flips `setHeavyFile` then `syncBufferLsp`); threshold via `editor.setLargeFileThreshold` + Settings ‚Üí Editor ‚Üí Performance. Bound memory (undo history is capped; loads are capped). **Undo granularity:** `boundedUndoManager` builds the RichTextFX manager with `UndoMerge.PAUSE` as the `preventMergeDelay` (idle break) and a `plainTextChanges` subscriber calls `UndoManager.preventMerge()` at word/whitespace/newline boundaries (pure `editor/UndoMerge.breakAfter`), so one `C-z` undoes a word/line instead of the whole contiguous burst RichTextFX would otherwise merge; split views share the document so both managers are broken together. **Undo History tool window** (`ui/UndoHistoryPanel`, id `undoHistory`, `Side.RIGHT`, `tool.undoHistory`/`M-g u`, buffer-gated; **registered default-hidden** via `register(tw, false)` ‚Äî the stripe button is off until the user enables it via Settings ‚Üí Tool Windows or `tool.undoHistory`, since the `undoHistory.jump` popup is the primary entry point): `editor/UndoHistory` keeps a capped (50) in-session list of full-document checkpoints captured on the `UndoMerge.PAUSE` debounce (`EditorBuffer.captureUndoCheckpoint`, skipped for huge/>1 MB files); the panel lists them newest-first (time + caret-line preview) and double-click/Enter calls `EditorBuffer.restoreUndoCheckpoint` (an undoable `replaceText`). A **popup alternative** ‚Äî command `undoHistory.jump` (`M-g v`; `MainController.undoHistoryPalette`, a `QuickOpen<UndoHistory.Checkpoint>` over the active buffer's `entriesNewestFirst()`, seeding a baseline when empty like the panel) ‚Äî opens the same checkpoints as a filterable in-scene overlay (label = caret-line preview, detail = `HH:mm:ss`); Enter restores. Session-only, finer-grained than save-based Local History; pure bits (`UndoHistory.add`/`lineAt`/`clamp`) unit-tested.
  - **Bound retained GPU textures.** JavaFX's Prism texture pool has a fixed ceiling (default 512 MB); exhausting it makes the render thread NPE (null `RTTexture`/mask texture) ‚Üí a black window ‚Äî seen only in the packaged build. So don't let GPU-backed resources grow with the number of open files: a background (non-selected) tab's buffer drops its minimap snapshot via `EditorBuffer.setRenderingActive(false)` (driven from the tab-selection + tabs-added listeners; `Minimap.setRenderingActive` nulls the cached snapshot and stops rendering, regenerating on show), and the `PreviewImageLoader`/`MermaidImages` image caches are **LRU-bounded** (not unbounded `ConcurrentHashMap`s) since each holds an `Image` (a pinned texture). The `dist` jpackage app (and `mvn javafx:run`) also raise the caps as a safety net (`-Dprism.maxvram=2G -Dprism.maxTextureSize=16384`). When adding any per-buffer Canvas/Image, make sure it's released or bounded.
  - **Packaged-runtime JVM tuning (footprint + install size).** The `dist` jpackage `<javaOptions>` (mirrored into the `javafx:run` options so dev == prod) cap the heap and GC: **`-Xmx2g`** (without it, jpackage inherits the default ergonomic max heap ‚âà ¬º of physical RAM ‚Äî multi-GB on a high-RAM box ‚Äî which lets GC-driven RSS balloon; 2g is predictable across the release matrix and safe for a 50 MB huge-file load + capped undo) and **`-XX:+UseSerialGC`** (a mostly-idle single-user editor on a small heap gets sub-ms pauses with no parallel GC-thread overhead ‚Äî lower idle RSS than the default G1; if large-file GC *hitching* ever shows up, generational ZGC is the smoothness-over-footprint alternative). The jpackage `<jLinkOptions>` strip the bundled runtime (`--strip-debug --no-man-pages --no-header-files --compress=zip-6`) ‚Üí smaller DMG/MSI/DEB + less mapped footprint. (`--strip-native-commands` is deliberately *omitted* from jLinkOptions ‚Äî `bin/java` must survive the jlink step for the AOT training run below; the `aot_build` helper deletes `bin/` itself afterward, reclaiming the same footprint. The runtime's `bin/` is never used at launch ‚Äî the jpackage native launcher starts the JVM via `libjli`, and every external tool (java/python/node/git/LSP/DAP) is resolved via the augmented PATH. **WINDOWS EXCEPTION (`aot_build.java` strips `bin/` non-Windows-only):** the Windows JDK layout puts the JVM *inside* `bin/` (`runtime\bin\server\jvm.dll` + the bootstrap `jli.dll`/`java.dll`/`jvm.cfg`/‚Ä¶), and `Editora.exe` loads `jvm.dll` from there ‚Äî so deleting `bin/` on Windows makes the launcher die with *"Failed to find JVM in ‚Ä¶\runtime directory"* (a shipped regression fixed by guarding the strip to non-Windows).
