On Windows the whole `bin/` is kept ‚Äî its launcher exes are a negligible footprint.) **AOT cache (JDK 25 Leyden) ‚Äî implemented, ~28%/‚âà300‚Äì480 ms faster cold start** (measured macOS: first-frame ~1060 ms ‚Üí ~760 ms; delivered-app wall delta ~480 ms): the build does a **two-phase jpackage** ‚Äî phase 1 (`prepare`) jlinks an `APP_IMAGE` into `target/aot-image` with `-XX:AOTCache=$APPDIR/editora.aot` baked into the launcher `.cfg`; then `scripts/aot_build.java` (run by `exec-maven-plugin` with the build JDK) **trains a full-GUI cache against the image's own runtime** (so archived classes match the shipped runtime, path-independently ‚Äî it maps after the install-dir move because the classes live in the jlinked `lib/modules`, keyed to the runtime image not absolute paths), writes `editora.aot` into `$APPDIR`, strips `bin/`, then either copies the image (APP_IMAGE builds) or wraps it into the installer via `jpackage --app-image` (DMG/MSI/DEB). **A *headless* trainer gives ‚âà0 win** ‚Äî the gain is JavaFX scene/control/CSS class loading, which only loads when a window renders; the training run is the real GUI driven by `-Deditora.aotTrainExit` (`WindowManager` renders the first frame, settles ~2.5 s for highlight-class coverage, then `System.exit`). On Linux the helper auto-wraps training in `xvfb-run` (release.yml installs `xvfb`+GTK/GL libs on the Linux legs); macOS/Windows runners use their session. **Fully failure-tolerant:** if training fails (no usable display on a runner, etc.) the build continues and ships without the cache ‚Äî a missing/invalid `-XX:AOTCache` file logs to stderr (invisible in the packaged app) and starts normally under the default `AOTMode=auto`. **Cost: the cache is ~60 MB**, so the installed image grows accordingly (the DMG/MSI/DEB compress it ‚Äî the DMG download stayed ~81 MB). **Prism pipeline order is per-OS** (the `${prism.pipeline}` property set in the `os-mac`/`os-windows`/`os-linux` profiles, passed as `-Dprism.order=${prism.pipeline}` to both the dist `<javaOptions>` and `javafx:run` `<options>`): **macOS = `mtl,es2,sw`** ‚Äî the **Metal** pipeline, added in **JavaFX 26**, which fixes the blank/garbled render-to-texture glitches the deprecated es2/OpenGL backend produced on Apple silicon (e.g. M-series: empty breadcrumb crumbs + tool-stripe icons); es2/sw stay as fallbacks since Metal is opt-in. **Windows = `d3d,es2,sw`** (must keep Direct3D ‚Äî a blanket `mtl,es2,sw` would strip d3d and lose Windows GPU accel). **Linux = `es2,sw`**. JavaFX 26 runs on JDK 24+, so the JDK stays **25**. Still a **commented-out opt-in** in the pom (DEVICE-TEST before enabling, touches correctness): JDK 25 **compact object headers** (`-XX:+UseCompactObjectHeaders`, experimental, ~10‚Äì20% live-heap cut ‚Äî note it changes the AOT cache's recorded layout, so retrain after enabling). *(Aside: `App.main` exits `--version`/`--help` via `System.exit(0)`, not a bare return ‚Äî launching this `Application` subclass in module mode pre-starts the FX toolkit, whose non-daemon keep-alive thread would otherwise hang the process after `main` returns.)*
  - **Assess and report the performance cost of every change.** For any implementation or bug fix, evaluate its cost on the hot paths (allocation per keystroke/scroll, added FX-thread work, extra layout/CSS passes, memory) and tell the user about it ‚Äî even if it's "negligible." If a change risks a regression, measure (e.g. the temporary `System.nanoTime` instrumentation used for the startup investigation) rather than guess.
- **Code style ‚Äî Palantir Java Format, enforced by Spotless.** All Java is auto-formatted with [Palantir Java Format](https://github.com/palantir/palantir-java-format) (a lambda-friendly, 120-col fork of google-java-format) via the `spotless-maven-plugin` (config in `pom.xml`; versions in the `${spotless.version}`/`${palantir.version}` properties). **Run `mvn spotless:apply` before committing** ‚Äî `mvn spotless:check` is bound to the `verify` phase, so `mvn verify`/`mvn package`/CI fail on unformatted code (the `mvn javafx:run`/`mvn compile` dev loop is deliberately left untouched). Pipeline: `removeUnusedImports` ‚Üí `palantirJavaFormat` ‚Üí `importOrder` ‚Üí `toggleOffOn`. **Import groups** (blank-line separated; longest-prefix wins, so `javafx` is *not* swallowed by `java`): JDK (`java`/`javax`) ‚Üí `javafx` ‚Üí everything else (third-party + `com.editora`) ‚Üí static imports last. Escape hatch for hand-aligned code: wrap it in `// spotless:off` ‚Ä¶ `// spotless:on`. Palantir 2.72.0+ supports JDK 25. The two tree-wide mechanical reformats are recorded in `.git-blame-ignore-revs` (enable locally once with `git config blame.ignoreRevsFile .git-blame-ignore-revs`; GitHub honors it automatically) so `git blame` skips them.
- **Code size ‚Äî soft limits, not hard gates.** Keep classes and methods small enough to hold in your head; these are review heuristics, not a build check. **Per class (target):** ‚â§ ~500 lines is ideal, ‚â§ ~1000 is fine; **~1000‚Äì1500** is acceptable only for a *genuinely cohesive subsystem* (e.g. `editor/EditorBuffer`, which coordinates one buffer's many overlays/managers ‚Äî treat it gently); **> ~2000 lines is a refactor smell** ‚Äî split it. **Per method (target):** ‚â§ ~50 lines ideal, **> ~100 is a smell** (extract helpers / a pure decision function). What actually matters is **responsibility count** and **cyclomatic complexity**, not raw line count ‚Äî a 600-line class doing one thing is healthier than a 300-line class doing five. When a class creeps over the line, the first move is to extract the *pure* logic (a decision/format/parse helper in its own class, unit-tested) and, for a whole feature, a **`CoordinatorHost`-style coordinator** (see the `ui/*Coordinator` classes). **`ui/MainController` is the known outlier** (~12k lines) and is being incrementally decomposed one feature at a time into `ui/*Coordinator` classes (External Tools, Macros, TODO, Search, Run done; Notes, Bookmarks, LSP, Debug pending) ‚Äî so **a new feature should be its own coordinator (or pure package), never bolted onto `MainController`**. No tooling enforces these numbers (JaCoCo gates *coverage*, not size); they're for human judgement during review and when deciding where new code lives.
- **Adding a feature = add a `Command`, and surface it in the command palette.** Every time we add a command or an applicable user-facing feature, it must be discoverable in the palette. Register it in `MainController.registerCommands()` and, if it needs a key, add a binding to `emacs.json`. The palette is populated from `CommandRegistry.all()`, so a properly registered command appears automatically ‚Äî never add a user-facing action that bypasses the registry. Toolbar buttons and the palette both dispatch through commands; don't wire UI handlers to logic directly when a command fits.
- **Every setting also needs a palette command** ‚Äî Editora is command-driven, so a Settings-window control (toggle, picker, font, path, number, ‚Ä¶) is **not** enough on its own; it must have a command-palette equivalent too. Register a command in `MainController.registerCommands()` that flips/prompts the **same** `Settings` field, persists (`requestSave()`), re-applies the feature (`applyGitSupport`/`applyLspSupport`/`applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`/‚Ä¶), and keeps an open Settings window in step via `SettingsWindow.syncAll()`. Toggles ‚Üí `view.toggle*` (master feature-enable toggles use a `view.`/`appearance.`/`debug.` prefix so the palette's feature-gating filter never hides them); values ‚Üí a `promptText` prompt or a `QuickOpen` picker; many per-item settings (e.g. the per-server LSP / per-adapter Debug commands) ‚Üí one grouped picker command. Reuse the generic helpers `toggleSetting`/`promptStringSetting`/`promptIntSetting`/`chooseSetting`, and add `command.<id>` + `command.<id>.desc` to all six i18n catalogs (the two shared status keys `status.settingToggled`/`status.settingChanged` reuse the command's own title). The 2026-06 sweep (PR #56) closed every gap ‚Äî keep parity when adding a setting.
- **Every user-facing string is localized ‚Äî never hardcode UI text.** Any new label, status/echo message, tooltip, dialog title/header/body, button, menu item, prompt, or placeholder must go through the i18n catalog: `import static com.editora.i18n.Messages.tr;` then `tr("some.key")` (or `tr("key", args‚Ä¶)` for `MessageFormat` parameters like `Saved {0}`) ‚Äî never pass a raw English literal to a JavaFX control. **Add the key to all six `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages[_<lang>].properties` files** (English base + `it/es/fr/pt/de`) with a real translation in each; `MessagesTest`'s key-parity check fails the build if any locale is missing a key. New `Command`s get their title for free via `Command.of(id, runnable)` + a `command.<id>` key. Only deliberate exceptions stay literal: technical tokens (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, detected language names, example URLs) and the pre-GUI `--help`/`--version` text. See the `i18n/` architecture bullet for the full system.
- **App icon / branding:** the source logo is `branding/editora-icon.svg`. Window-icon PNGs (16‚Äì512) live in `resources/com/editora/icons/` (loaded into `stage.getIcons()` in `App`; also the About-dialog logo). Native-installer icons `branding/editora.{icns,ico,png}` are generated from the SVG (rsvg-convert + iconutil + a small ICO writer) and passed to jpackage via `${jpackage.icon}`, set per-OS in the OS-activated profiles. Regenerate after editing the SVG.
- **Context-menu icons:** **every right-click `MenuItem` carries a leading icon** (`MenuItem.setGraphic(...)`). UI-package menus (tab strip + Welcome close in `MainController.installTabMenu`, `ProjectPanel`, `GitPanel`, `BookmarksPanel`, `NotesPanel`, `MessageLogPopup`, `FileBreadcrumb`) use `com.editora.ui.Icons` directly; the **editor** package's menus (`EditorBuffer.installContextMenu` + `showPreviewContextMenu`) can't depend on `ui`, so they use **`com.editora.editor.MenuIcons`** ‚Äî a package-local mirror of `Icons` (same Material 24dp single-path glyphs, `toolbar-icon` style class, 0.8 scale) holding only the glyphs those two menus need (cut/copy/paste/undo/redo/selectAll, markdown bold/italic/strike/code/link, LSP goto-def/refs/hover, spellcheck/add/block, note/run/download/print); the Run item reuses `FoldManager.runGlyph()`. Icons are colored via the global `.toolbar-icon` rule (`-color-fg-muted`, theme-aware), so they track light/dark for free ‚Äî **no new CSS**. When adding a context menu or item, give every item a `setGraphic` glyph (reuse an existing one where no exact match exists, e.g. the close-tab X across all close-variants). The recent-files toolbar **MenuButton** dropdown is not a right-click menu and is intentionally excluded (its entries already carry an inline remove-icon); the snippet **choice** dropdown lists content values, not commands, and is likewise excluded.
- **File-type icons:** **`com.editora.ui.FileIcons`** maps a file name to a small monochrome glyph reflecting its type, shown wherever a file is listed: editor tabs (`MainController.updateTabMeta`), the `ProjectPanel` tree (file rows; folders keep `Icons.project()`), the `FileFinder` file/folder pickers, the `Switcher` cell, and the **Open Files** / **Recent Files** `QuickOpen` pickers (via the new optional `QuickOpen.setItemIcon(Function<T,Node>)`). The pure, unit-tested **`FileIcons.iconKeyFor(name)`** resolves a name ‚Üí glyph key ‚Äî non-language extensions first (image png/jpg/svg/‚Ä¶‚Üí`image`, `pdf`, archive zip/jar/‚Ä¶‚Üí`archive`, csv/tsv‚Üí`table`, `*.lock`, txt/log‚Üí`text`), else `LanguageRegistry.forFileName(name)`'s language id ‚Üí key (java/python/js/ts/go/php/ruby/c/cpp/csharp/kotlin/html/css/markdown/yaml/json/xml‚Üícode/shell/powershell+batchfile‚Üíterminal/dockerfile/terraform/mermaid/sql‚Üístorage/ini+toml+‚Ä¶‚Üísettings/rust+lua+groovy+http‚Üícode); unknown ‚áí `generic` ‚Üí the existing `Icons.fileSheet()` fallback (so unrecognized files look exactly as before). **`forFileName(name)`** turns the key into a fresh `Icons.of(path)` node ‚Äî glyphs are single-path SVGs in the `toolbar-icon` style (theme-aware, no per-theme overrides, **no new CSS**). Brand logos are vendored from **Simple Icons** (CC0); category glyphs from **Material Design Icons** (Apache-2.0) ‚Äî attributed in `NOTICE`. `Icons.of(...)` was made package-private so `FileIcons` (same package) reuses it. To add/adjust a mapping: extend the `iconKeyFor` switch + add the glyph path to `FileIcons.PATHS` + a `FileIconsTest` case. *(No new dependency; glyphs are inlined path strings, like the existing browser logos.)*
- **Bundled fonts:** five monospace families ship under `resources/com/editora/fonts/<family>/` (Regular/Bold/Italic/BoldItalic TTFs; Fira Code has no italic), **plus Inter** (sans-serif, `fonts/inter/`) as the Markdown **preview + PDF prose** font. `Fonts.load()` registers them all via `Font.loadFont` at the very start of `App.start` (before any CSS), so they resolve by family name regardless of the OS. `Fonts.BUNDLED` (JetBrains Mono first = default) is the **monospace** editor-font picker list and deliberately **excludes Inter** (Inter isn't an editor font); it's listed ahead of the system monospaced families in the Settings font picker. Inter is the preview prose font on **all platforms** (`.markdown-preview .md-text` in `app.css` ‚Äî pinned explicitly because raw `Text` nodes don't reliably inherit the scene font, and because the macOS chrome's logical "System" family can't be bold-rasterized cleanly by JavaFX) and the PDF prose font (`MarkdownPdfWriter`). They're plain resources (no `module-info`/moditect change) and are picked up by the `dist` build automatically. Attributed in `NOTICE` (all OFL-1.1).
- **Theming:** AtlantaFX is the user-agent stylesheet and themes standard controls (`Themes`, set via `Application.setUserAgentStylesheet`). It does **not** style the RichTextFX `CodeArea` ‚Äî editor surface, line-number gutter, and syntax token colors live in `styles/app.css` + `styles/syntax.css` (the **Primer Light** defaults). **Editor color themes** (`EditorThemes`) layer an override stylesheet from `styles/editor-themes/<name>.css` onto the scene *after* those defaults (Primer Light = no override); `MainController.applyEditorTheme` swaps that sheet on the scene and sets each buffer's current-line highlight color (RichTextFX's line-highlight fill is set in code, not CSS). The editor theme follows the AtlantaFX theme (`EditorThemes.defaultFor`) until the user picks one (`Settings.editorThemeUserSet`). Token rules must stay the compound `.text.<class>` form ‚Äî see the header comment in `syntax.css`. The **Project tool window file tree** is themed via two looked-up CSS colors `-project-folder-color`/`-project-file-color` (defined on `.project-tree` in `app.css`, defaulting to AtlantaFX accent/muted); each editor theme overrides them, so a new editor theme should add a `.project-tree { -project-folder-color: ‚Ä¶; -project-file-color: ‚Ä¶; }` rule. **Bundled community themes:** beyond the 7 built-in AtlantaFX themes (Primer/Nord/Cupertino/Dracula), `Themes` also lists 19 MIT-licensed community themes from the DLSC `atlantafx-themes` collection (Blue/Navy/Army L/D, the four seasonal L/D sets, Autumn/Browny/News/Yacht ‚Äî the GitHub colorblind/tritanopia variants are excluded on purpose). Their control-theme CSS is **vendored** under `styles/atlantafx-themes/<name>.css` (self-contained AtlantaFX user-agent stylesheets; `url()`s resolve to JDK modena assets) and served by `Themes.BundledTheme` ‚Äî a small `atlantafx.base.theme.Theme` impl **kept in `com.editora.ui`** so `theme.getClass().getResource(...)` finds the vendored CSS in *this* module (a `Theme.of(...)` instance would resolve against atlantafx-base and return null). `Themes.BUNDLED` (name ‚Üí {css base, dark, bg-default hex}) drives `themeFor`/`backgroundFor`. **The matching editor themes all share one file** ‚Äî `styles/editor-themes/adaptive.css` ‚Äî whose `.editor-area`/`.text.<class>`/`.project-tree` rules are written entirely in the theme's own `-color-*` semantic variables (keyword‚Üí`danger-fg`, string‚Üí`success-fg`, number‚Üí`accent-fg`, type‚Üí`warning-fg`, function‚Üí`accent-emphasis`, comment‚Üí`fg-muted`, ‚Ä¶), so one palette adapts to every theme with no per-theme syntax file. `EditorThemes` still needs per-theme **code-driven** colors that CSS vars can't reach (startup background, current-line highlight, minimap block/viewport), taken from each theme's `-color-bg-default`/`-color-fg-default`/`-color-bg-subtle`/`-color-fg-muted`/`-color-accent-emphasis`. **To add another AtlantaFX theme:** vendor its `.css`, add a `Themes.BUNDLED` entry + the name to both `Themes.NAMES`/`EditorThemes.NAMES`, and add `EditorThemes` map entries (CSS‚Üí`adaptive`, plus the 5 code-driven colors). `ThemesTest` guards that every theme resolves a loadable stylesheet + has a matching editor theme + parseable colors. Community-theme CSS is MIT (attributed in `NOTICE`). **User-defined themes** (`ui/UserThemes`, loaded once in `App.start` via `UserThemes.load(configDir)` before the theme is applied; palette command `theme.reloadUserThemes` re-scans): two folders under the config dir ‚Äî **`themes/*.css`** = full AtlantaFX control themes (each becomes an app theme *and* an adaptive editor theme, exactly like the bundled community ones ‚Äî served via a file-URL `BundledTheme` + `adaptive.css`, with code-driven colors parsed from the CSS's `-color-*`), and **`editor-themes/*.css`** = hand-authored editor overrides (editor-theme picker only, served by the file URL). **A user theme file must declare at least one `-color-*`/`-fx-*`** (`looksLikeStylesheet`) ‚Äî every `.css` in the folder is offered, so an empty/half-written one otherwise became a pickable theme that strips AtlantaFX from the app ‚Äî and **`parseColor` follows a token defined by reference** (`-color-bg-default: -color-dark-1;`, bounded to `MAX_VAR_HOPS`, cycle-safe) and won't match a longer token that merely starts with it: the bundled themes and upstream AtlantaFX all use literal hex, so a reference-style theme silently parsed as *no colour* ‚Üí white bg + `dark=false` ‚Üí dark chrome around a white editor. The picker/combo lists now come from `Themes.names()` / `EditorThemes.names()` (built-ins + user), not the static `NAMES` (kept as the built-in list); `normalize`/`defaultFor`/`stylesheetFor`/the color accessors consult `UserThemes.controlThemes()`/`editorThemes()`. The theme **name is the file base name Title-Cased** (`my-theme.css` ‚Üí "My Theme"); a name colliding with a built-in is skipped. `UserThemes.titleCase`/`parseColor`/`baseName` are pure/unit-tested; a user theme's `file:` URL passes straight through `Themes.stylesheetFor`'s `hasUrlScheme` check.
- **Tests** are mostly **pure logic** (keymap resolution, command registry, config merge, highlighting spans), plus a small **headless-JavaFX harness** for toolkit-bound `ui/` behavior (see below). Prefer extracting pure decision helpers and unit-testing those (it's faster + needs no toolkit) ‚Äî but real controller behavior (Zen toggling chrome, Simple-mode stripping, tab/window lifecycle) is now covered end-to-end via the FX harness. **Coverage:** `mvn test` runs the JaCoCo agent and writes a report to `target/site/jacoco/index.html` (+ `jacoco.xml`); `mvn verify` additionally runs a JaCoCo **`check`** that enforces a per-package LINE-coverage **floor** on the well-covered pure packages (migration¬∑diff ‚â•0.90, config ‚â•0.86, template¬∑editorconfig ‚â•0.82, completion¬∑http¬∑pdf ‚â•0.70 ‚Äî see the `jacoco-check` execution in `pom.xml`), so their coverage can't silently regress. Floors sit comfortably below current levels (a regression net, not a target) ‚Äî **when you raise a package's coverage, ratchet its floor up**. `ui`/`editor` are still **deliberately ungated** (the FX harness covers only a few % of `ui`'s ~16.7k lines so far ‚Äî add a floor only once coverage is meaningful). The dev loop (`mvn javafx:run`/`compile`) is unaffected ‚Äî the check runs only at `verify`/`package`. The cheapest way to raise `ui` coverage is still to extract pure decision helpers (effective-visibility/gating predicates, caret-navigation math, path keying, ‚Ä¶) and unit-test those ‚Äî see `ui/Chrome`, `editor/TextNav`, `config/PathKeys`.
  - **Sample corpus (`samples/`)** ‚Äî a curated, feature-organized set of small text samples for **manual** smoke-testing/demos (one subdir per feature: `syntax/` per language, `folding/`, `indent/`, `markdown/`, `mermaid/`, `todo/`, `spell/`, `search/`, `editorconfig/` (hermetic, `root=true`), `http/`, `log/`, `diff/`, `encodings/`). It's a **human aid**, not part of the behavioral suite; `samples/README.md` is the manifest and `SamplesCorpusTest` only guards that the manifest ‚Üî committed files stay in sync + the core languages each have a syntax sample (add/remove a sample ‚áí update the README or the test fails). Large/perf inputs are **generated** by `java scripts/GenSamples.java` (a JDK 25 compact source file, run from the repo root) into the git-ignored `samples/perf/` (never committed ‚Äî keeps history lean). A scoped root `.gitattributes` marks `samples/encodings/**` + `samples/diff/conflict.txt` `-text` so git never normalizes the encoding/EOL/conflict-marker bytes, and `samples/**` `linguist-vendored`. Samples are inert-by-name (no real `.gitignore`/secrets; the EditorConfig fixture is sandboxed with `root=true`). Spotless only formats `src/{main,test}/java`, so sample `.java` files are left untouched.
  - **Headless-FX harness** (`src/test/java/com/editora/ui/`): **TestFX** (`testfx-core`/`testfx-junit5`) drives only the toolkit **lifecycle** (`FxToolkit.registerPrimaryStage()`) over **JavaFX 26's built-in Headless Glass platform** (`-Dglass.platform=Headless`, part of `javafx.graphics` since 26 ‚Äî no Monocle jar, no native libs) ‚Äî so FX tests run headless on CI with **no display/xvfb**. The harness never drives the TestFX **robot** (no `clickOn`/key simulation ‚Äî everything goes through `runOnFx`/`callOnFx` + reflection), so the prototype headless platform's input/rendering limitations don't apply, and TestFX needs no changes despite not yet officially adopting the new platform. All FX tests are `@Tag("fx")`; run the pure suite alone with `./mvnw test -DexcludedGroups=fx`. `FxTestSupport` boots the toolkit once (Headless platform + `Fonts.load`/`Messages.init`/AtlantaFX UA sheet/classloader pin) and exposes `runOnFx`/`callOnFx` + reflection helpers (`field`/`invoke`/`call`) to read private `@FXML` nodes and invoke private methods (tests run on the **classpath** as the unnamed module, so `setAccessible` is unrestricted). `FxWindowFixture` builds a real window via `WindowManager.buildWindowForTest()` (a package-private seam mirroring `buildWindow`) against a temp config dir ‚Äî **if that boot path changes, the fixture/seam must track it**. The **surefire config** is what makes this work: `<useModulePath>false</useModulePath>` (classpath mode), the headless system properties (`glass.platform=Headless`, `prism.order=sw`), and **`<argLine>@{argLine}</argLine>`** ‚Äî the `@{argLine}` token is mandatory so JaCoCo's injected coverage agent (set via the `argLine` property) survives; a plain `<argLine>` would clobber it.

## Packaging note (important)

RichTextFX is a **personal fork** (`io.github.adriandeleon:richtextfx`, vendored in the in-project
`m2-repo/`, source at github.com/adriandeleon/RichTextFX) that adds VS Code‚Äìstyle **multiple cursors +
Alt+drag column/box selection** via a self-contained `org.fxmisc.richtext.multi.MultiCaretController.install(area)`
add-on (a layered wellbehaved `InputMap`, gated on `MultiCaretManager.hasExtras()` so it's transparent with
one caret). **`EditorBuffer`** installs it on `area`/`area2` via `setMultiCaretEnabled(...)` (gated by
`Settings.multiCaret`, default on; pushed by `MainController.applyMultiCaret`), exposes
`hasMultipleCarets()` + delegating `addCaretNextOccurrence`/`addCaretAbove`/`addCaretBelow`/`collapseCarets`
(palette commands `edit.addCaret*`/`edit.collapseCarets`, `view.toggleMultiCaret` ‚Äî **no keymap bindings**:
gestures are mouse + Esc, native to the fork). Because Editora's area-level KEY filters (auto-indent/close,
snippets, completion, view paging) are capture-phase *filters* that run before the fork's node InputMap,
each one early-returns (no consume) via `multiCaretActiveOn(a)` when that area has extra carets, so editing
fans out to all carets. *Known limitation:* Emacs movement chords (`C-f`/`C-n`/‚Ä¶) are resolved by the
scene-level `KeyDispatcher` on the primary caret and don't fan out ‚Äî use arrows for multi-caret movement.
To update the fork: rebuild it, copy the new `richtextfx-<version>.{jar,pom}` into `m2-repo/`, bump
`<richtextfx.version>`. RichTextFX and its transitive deps (`reactfx`, `flowless`, `undofx`, `wellbehavedfx`)
are **automatic modules**, which `jlink` cannot link. The `moditect-maven-plugin` in
the `dist` profile injects explicit `module-info` descriptors into them. If you bump
RichTextFX or add a dep it uses, you may need to adjust those descriptors' `requires`
(e.g. several of them need `javafx.controls` for `IndexRange`). Use RichTextFX
**0.11.7+** ‚Äî earlier versions are incompatible with JavaFX 25.

tm4e (the syntax engine) ships as the NetBeans repackaging
`org.netbeans.external:org.eclipse.tm4e.core-0.14.0:RELEASE260` (tm4e is not on
Maven Central). Its Oniguruma backend (`org.jruby.joni:joni`, `org.jruby.jcodings:jcodings`)
and `com.google.code.gson:gson` are already proper modules, but tm4e core is an
automatic module, so `moditect` injects a `module-info` for it too. The NetBeans
jar is also **code-signed**, and `jlink` rejects signed modular jars ‚Äî the `dist`
profile's antrun step strips `META-INF/*.SF,*.RSA,*.DSA,*.EC` before linking.

**Headless FX testing ‚Äî built-in platform (no Monocle).** As of **JavaFX 26** the headless Glass backend for the
FX test harness is the **built-in Headless platform** that ships inside `javafx.graphics` (`-Dglass.platform=Headless`,
set in the surefire `<systemPropertyVariables>`). **No jar, no native libs, no separate download, nothing vendored** ‚Äî
it's part of the JavaFX runtime, so it can never go stale on a JavaFX bump. This **replaced** the previously
self-built **Monocle** backend (`io.github.adriandeleon:openjfx-monocle`, which had to be rebuilt from the OpenJFX
sources on every JavaFX bump and vendored in `m2-repo/`) ‚Äî that whole rebuild ritual and its vendored artifacts are
gone. The new platform is officially a **prototype** in 26, but the harness only uses TestFX's `FxToolkit` to **boot
the toolkit** and never drives the robot (input/clicks) or renders/snapshots in tests, so the prototype's
rendering/input limitations don't apply (and TestFX needs no changes despite not yet adopting it ‚Äî see
[TestFX #819](https://github.com/TestFX/TestFX/issues/819)). No `module-info`/jlink impact ‚Äî it's test scope only and
never on the runtime path. *(If a future need ever requires real headless rendering or robot input under the
prototype, Monocle could be re-vendored, but as of 26 it isn't needed.)*
